January 28, 1959 To whom it may concern On this date, January 28, 1959 I visited
Kaysam Corporation, Paterson, N.J. My former employer with the intent of
determining if they would be helpful to me in producing models of squeeze and
novelty toy ideas I have consented for products made of dry molded latex and/or
rotational or slush molded vinyl or the like. The basic ideas which I sketched
and described to both Carl Hotstein and Abe Duncan are hereby recorded primarily
because, after describing them to Duncan, he discussed my problem with Mr.
Ernest Gelles, president of the company without asking me if he should do so. He
told me that he had informed Gelles that I had some new ideas in squeeze toys
but did not go into the exact details. However, Carl Hotstein later remarked to
me that Abe Duncan cannot be trusted to maintain confidence. Basically the
designs evolve about a toy having a central body member or portion made out of a
dipped latex bellows, bellows or a rotational or slushed molded bellows portion.
A design is illustrated on page 7 consists of a toy (squeeze novelty, crib or
play toy) having a body with three portions, an upper body portion 12, a central
body portion 14 which is shaped like a bellows which extends at its lower end to
a lower body portion 16 or stand which may be molded integral with 14 or secured
thereto the tower end of 14 or of 16 may be secured to a Lenore Waldmeyer Jan
28, 1959 J.B. Silstein Sept. 5, 1959

upper body portion 12 hollow flexible molded plastic vinyl latex on
polyetheyline central body portion 14 bellows shape noisemaker lower body
portion 16 (stand (weighted, feet, suction cup) clamp, etc opening 18

### Page 4
clamp, suction cup or other device for securing it to a surface, railing or part
of a crib or handle. The bellows is of such a characteristic that it will
ordinarily remain in the expanded state and support the upper body portion 12
but may be easily deflected to collapse or squeeze together and create a noise
by expelling air thru an opening 18 (such as at the bottom wall) having a
noisemaker therin. Reference is may to my copending application entitled
noisemaking Toys and particularly to Figs. 20 and 21 for details of this
construction in the fabrication of a bellows noisemaker. Jerome Lemelson Jan 28
1959 Witnessed and read by Lenore Waldmeyer Jan 28, 959 Witnessed read &
understood by Jacob B. Gilstein Sept-5, 1959 Witnessed and read by Eleanor
Campbell 10/23/59

August. 4. 1959 Record of Conception: The following product and packaging ideas
will be incorporated into patent application and will, in the coming months, be
delivered to Johnson and Johnson. I. Brush Covering - This was conceived a
number of years ago and the patent specification (first draft) worked out last
winter. It consists of several novel designs for ~~ pla ~~ covers for the
bristles or tufts of various types of brushes. The covers are preferably molded
of plastic and snap over or screw onto a formed section of the brush base
adjacent the bristle. II. Single Shot (liquid, cream, or powder) Dispensers It
has been conceived by me to provide a low cost dispenser or package for flowable
material for possibly for a single application of a liquid such as an
antiseptic, nose drops, face cream, ointment, burn salv oil (baby oil, ~~ it ~~
machine oil), medicine (spray), ~~ or the like ~~ powder or the like. These
dispensers are preferably made of plastic (from 2 heat sealed sheets (.001 to
.005 " thick) or thin walled tubing Conceived designs as follows

cream or powder. The closure is preferably made of a flattened tube or two
sheets of plastic material, metal foil or laminates Read & UNDERSTOOD By J.B.

nostril, the nose portion 16 is preferably provided narrow enough to effect said
insertion and the material of 10 on both sides of 16, referred to by the
notation 10a and 10b, is preferably removed by die-cutting. A semi-circular
die-cut such as 22 may suffice to provide 16 in a small enough cross-section for
insertion into its intended cavity. To dispense the material held in 12, the
wall thereof must be severed and this may be accomplished in one of several
manners. While the end of nose 16 may be cut off with an implement such as a
scissors, if the container is to be carried on a person for use when the need
arises, it is preferable that a simpler method of opening the nose wall be
provided. Quick opening may be effected in one of a number of manners. The ~~
melt ~~ opening means illustrated in Fig. 11 utilizes the tearing of the
material of one wall of 16 by means of a tear strip 20 which is a narrow band of
flexible or rigid plastic, 3/32 to 1/4 inches wide, which preferably has a
tensile strength greater than that of the material of the wall of 16. In Fig. 1
the tear strip 20 is shown welded or heat sealed to the outer surface of ~~ the
~~ one wall of 16, which weld is provided in a manner such that when the tear
strip is pulled upward from 16 or longitudinally relative to 16, a small Read

distance beyond the end of 16. The tubing may be closed at one end (the outer)

Electric Razor Design Monitone Universal HOLLOW TUBULAR CYLINDER Oct. 9, 1959

Fig. 1 Figs 1 illustrates in partial cross-section details of the improved
electric razor head in partial cross-section. The razor 10 has a molded plastic
casing 12 of conventional design and made in two or more parts assembled with
fasteners with internally mounted components secured to said housery and
consisting of a rechargable battery 27 which is electrically connected thru an
externally operative switch 30 to a d.c. motor 25 for operating the cutting
components of the razor. The shaft 25' of motor 25 is coupled to a gear train 24
having an output or drive gear 24'. The motor, battery and gear train are ~~
separded from ~~ secured is separated from the head section 11 of the razor by
means of a wall or partition 26. Cutting is accomplished by means of a rotary
cutter 22 which is a thin walled cylinder, preferably made from stainless steel
~~ or ~~ tubing having a wall thickness less than .015 inches. Force filled into
the end portions of the cyclinder 22 are shaft pins 16 and 21. The ends of these
pins are supported in rotational bearing by means of bearings 15 and 20 which

Gilstein Nov 1, 1959 Record of Conception Some time prior to this date I have
conceived of the method and apparatus for providing printed decorations on blow
molded plastic articles by printing on the sheet or sheet of plastic from which
the article is made, then heating it to ~~ near ~~ formable state as it feeds
between mold halves without destroying printing, registering it in adjacent mold
halves and closing mold halves when in registration while blowing the sheets
outward with air. The printing may be effected on either those surfaces which
form the inside or outside of the article. A photoelectric relay scanning the LW
11/13/59 EJW 11/13/59

printing (positional marks) may be used to effect longitudinal registration of
printed matter. Jerome H Lemelson

### Page 12
Nov 6, 1959 Concerning the above idea, an edge line or lines ~~ scann ~~ printed
on the sheet or sheets of plastic to be blow molded may be used for lateral
registration. The correction of the position of a photoelectric cell (error
signal derived in change in position when ~~ fo ~~ the motor driving the mount
for the cell laterally to maintain it in alignment with said line) may be used
to shift either the means guiding the sheets to align it with the mold or shift
the mold in a lateral position so that the printed matter on the sheet will be
exactly registered in the molded product. To protect the printed matter from
distortion when the sheet is blown into the mold, it may be provided between the
surface of one or both sheets. One method of providing it between surfaces is to
coat or laminate the same or other (sheet) material on the printed surface of
the sheet or to provide said printed illustration on the inside surface of the
sheet laminated thereto. Another method is to utilize a sheet of plastic in
white a photographic image has been reproduced and blow mold this material after
carefully heating to semi-molten state. Here are several article ideas which
together with the above, I intend to file patent application on. Imitation

.025 to .010 inches in thickness having a second sheet 3 (~~ .0005 to .002"
thick)of a highly durable plastic material such as polyvinyl fluoride bonded and
laminated to the outside surface of 1, the outer surface 3' of 3 being that
which is exposed to the atmosphere. A multi-colored transparent or translucent
design (simulating a stained glass window pattern) may be provided at the
interface 4 between 2 and 3 by printing with translucent or transparent ink on
either the inside face of 4 or the outside face of 2. The notation 2b refers to
a vacuum  or ? ~~ formed or molded ridge formation in the sheet 2 or assembly 1
simulating the metal joining the sections of stained glass and the illustration
4" printed at the interface 4 is preferably black material to simulated the iron
metal which joins sections of stained glass in a window frame. The inside
surface 2' of 2 may or may not be coated with a protective plastic layer such as
acrylonitrile plastic or PVT film itself The above lamination and decorative
means may be applied to windows of any design  and it is conceived that many new
and interesting shapes may be provided. For example, the ribbed formation 2b may
have different shapes and may be limited in its length. It may represent a jewel
sch as a ruby or saphire (its shape being integrally molded or vacuum formed and

P.V.F. spray Nov. 17, 1959 The following idea was conceived by me some time ago
for possible development. It is conceived to form a dispersion of polyvinyl
fluoride plastic having a characteristic such that it may be aerosoled (sprayed)
cold / dispensed from a can by means of pressure generated by Freon or the like,
or by means of conventional spray equipment. It is also conceived to form a
dispersion of P.V.F. and P.V.C. combined in the proportions necessary to impart
the desired characteristics to the resulting film or coating derived when
sprayed on a surface. I mentioned the above to Marvin Margolis today who I asked
not to mention it to any of the representatives of Taussig Paint Company until I
am ~~ n ~~ able to obtain sample ~~ from ~~ of P.V.F. from du Pont and
experiment with in an attempt to form a dispersion which may be sprayed. I asked
Harold Wilson about dispersions today and he mentioned use of colloid mill,
fluid energy mill and supersonic homogenizer Also conceived some time ago were
several methods of applying Teflon coatings to metal surfaces, viz. (1) First
clean surface, (2) then apply an adhesive layer or coating such as Eastman 910
adhesive, Pliobond or other strong adhesive which will tenaciously adhere to the
surface to be coated with the plastic (Teflon, etc), (3) Then apply the
Teflon/dispersion, preferably air-drying as produced by Acheson Colloids, (urea
plastic base) which does not require heat. If Eastman 910 is to be used, since
pressure starts polymerization this may be effected by mechanically compressing
the surface of the article (if sheet by applying a Teflon surfaced roller
thereto under pressure) or by means of pressure applied as one or a series of
shock waves impinged against the surface of the article or the article may be
vibrated itself with sufficient force to start polymerization of the adhesive.

Improvements to ultrasonic cleaning devices of my pending patent application
entitled "Ultrasonic Apparatus" particularly as applied to cleaning teeth and
the like: water is automatically drawn off when control switch is released
turning off energy. Witnessed & understood by me. Paul Cohen 1/25/60 Fig. 1 The
apparatus of Fig.1 at the left is preferably the end of a hand tool 10
consisting of an elongated barrel or tubular body 12 the end 12' of which is
preferably made of a transparent rigid plastic or glass. Secured by means of a
clamping ring 18 to the end of 12 is a nozzle or annular tip 16 made of flexible
transparent plastic such as flexible polyvinyl chloride or transparent silicone
rubber. Extending thru the end of 12 is an elongated rigid rod 14 the end 15 of
which is a tool tip. The rod 14 is magnetically or electrically coupled to a
transducing means part of Witnessed and understood by me. Ernest J Waldmeyer Nov
19, 1959 Ernest A Waldmeyer Nov 19 1959 JMB 12/5/5 19 Nov 59 JBG JPS 12/20/59
Witnessed & understood  DDS 1/16/60

### Page 25
which 21 is shown which when energized by a source of alternating current causes
the rod 14 and tip 15 to vibrate by means of magnetostriction. The end of 15
when brought into contact with a surface thru the opening 17 of 16 and and
vibrated thereagainst will effect, an abrading acted on said surface. A fluid
inlet line 19 and outlet line 20 are connected to openings in the wall of 12 and
fluid may be circulated thereby thru the interior 13 of the jacket or duct 12.
The rod 14 is preferably rearward or inward of the plane of opening 17 so that
if it is desired to get the tool or tip 15 into a cavity this may be effected
without interference from 17. However, 17 may be of various external end shapes,
the selection of which will result from a consideration of the type and shape of
the surface against which the tool is to be abutted. By making the end 12 and/or
16 transparent, the operator may visually note the condition of the surface
against which it abuts. Other features of the invention include in addition to a
simple and rapid adjustment of the longitudinal position of 15, a rapid (push
button) means for varying or stopping and starting the flow of liquid thru the
chamber. The end 200 of 20 is shown positioned near the ~~tip ~~ end of tool 15
so that liquid will circulate properly and material removed by 15 will be
immediately withdrawn. Also conceived, and reference is made to my copending
application for Ultrasonic Apparatus is the use of a pressure switch in the
chamber 13 which may operate to automatically stop the flow of liquid thru the
chamber in the event there is an interruption in the seal established between
the face of 17 and the work. J. Lemelson Nov. 18, 1959 Witnessed, Read &

Also being worked on at this time (spec. and claims partially finished) our
designs I have conceived some time ago for a trailer or a truck (body) having a
plurality 12/29/59 MW EJW 1/19/60 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY

of gravity conveyors arranged in a tier like array and adapted to be
simultaneously tilted or pivoted relative to the horizontal to assume one of two
positions or a plurality of positions. If a plurality of products of defined
shape are to be loaded and removed from one end (such as the rear) then by
tilting all conveyors downward towards the front end (on the vehicle body) the
products introduced on to each conveyor will flow

### Page 34
towards the front end and stack-up one behind the other. By reversing the tilt
angle (past the horizontal) no slope is down towards the rear end, products on
each conveyor will be urged rearward by gravity By providing a gate at the
loading end of each conveyor and selectively operating each gate (when a lift
truck or conveyor is adjacent the conveyor) each conveyor may be selectively
unloaded. J Lemelson Dec. 7/11/1959 The following products were suggested by me

Lemelson General information has been obtained from the General Electric Company
on the so call TPR, thermoplastic recording process developed and invented by
Dr. William C. Glen for the GE Research Laboratory. A converging electron beam,
modulated by a picture signal or other signal is focused on a tape laminate
consisting of a base, similar to a standard motion picture film, 6C 1/25/60 LW
1/25/60 RW 2/1/60 RSK PC 1/25/60 2/20/60

### Page 55
means to move in a predetermined path (focusing at or near the surface to be
coated) by means of conventional beam deflection means which may be regulated by
means of an analog signal reproduced from magnetic tape or other means in
predetermined time relation to reproduction of other control signals; The
electron beam may also be focused along a predetermined axis for a predetermined
time with said material flowing there thru after the work is automatically
controlled in its movement and position by the automatic controller; The
material to be coated may be a semi-conductor conductor or insulator in any
desired pattern ~~ dicated by ~~ determined by movement of the beam and/or the
position of a mask of any shape or other means between the beam and work. A mask
held stationery or movable, having a plurality of openings any one of which the
beam may be directed thru by control of its deflection, is also conceived. The
beam may also be generated per se prior to introduction of the coating material
to condition (heat or erode) the surface of the work to be coated and/or
generated after wating to work to effect the material deposited on the work. By
first introducing one material into the beam and then a second without moving
the beam or work, alternate layers of material may be built up. By automatic
control of the focal point and/or the degree of divergences as well as power
input to the beam, the area to be coated (width of a line of coating for example
as beam is moved) may be controlled to effect the formation of such surface
patterns as line conductors, resistors, etc: A servo or servos may also be
provided and automatically controlled to select and/or position different areas
of a mask or different masks in alignment with a stationery or movable beam.

T.P.R. for machine control

### Page 56
To improve the visibility of the T.P.R. image so that it appears as a print (a)
Stain the surface with a translucent liquid, wash (controlled). Do this while
T.P.R. is cooling. (b) Dust the cooling thermoplastic surface with particles
such as carbon. (c) Sputter a metal onto the T.P.R. film wrinkle surface. To
control the deposition of material on a surface of T.P.R. thermoplastic
material, create a predetermined wrinkle pattern in said thermoplastic layer by
means of T.P.R. equipment. Then apply a fluid material to the wrinkled surface
or spatter it thereon. Remove ~~ that ~~ all or part of the material covering
the outer surfaces ~~ forma ~~ of the formations by washing, the flow of a fluid
thereover, vibration, mechanical abrading or other means while retaining the
fluid material in the indentions whereafter it solidifies. The material retained
in the indentations may be used as conducting or semi conducting elements of
circuits, or to serve other functions. For example, it may be a phospor material
to be used in electronic display devices or in switching and computing elements.

The apparatus illustrated (on p.60 in Fig. 1) is an electron discharge device
having an electron gun 32 mounted in a ~~ master ~~ main housing 12 the end of
which is openable by means of a valve 18 to permit communication ~~ of ~~
between the interior volume 32' of the electron gun ~~ with ~~ and a surface of
a work-member 40 so that the energy generated by the gun may be directed against
said surface - A sealing ring 22 or washer on the end portion of the housing 12
seals off the volume 32' from the atmosphere so that when the valve ~~ is ~~ 18
is opened with the gun in abutment with the work, most of the vacuum created in
32' by vacuum pump 26 will be maintained; the only a loss of vacuum being in the
volume 32" between valve 18 and the surface of the work piece 40. The notation
30 refers to a support for the housing 12 which extends to any known manual or
automatically controlled handling mechanism for prepositioning the assembly 10
with the opening 32" in alignment with a predetermined area of the work piece
40. The notation 34 refers to a means for focusing the electron beam Be at or
near the surface of the work. The device of Fig. 1 may be used to perform the
following functions. (a) Irradiating a specific portion of an area of a
workpiece with a high energy ~~ elect ~~ beam focused on a predetermined point
or small portion of the area for heating, welding, or otherwise effecting the
material thereof. (b) By modulating the beam, if the surface 40' is coated,
covered or abutted with a thermoplastic film (such as described on p. 1870 of
vol.30 no. 12, Dec. 1959 issue of Journal of Applied Physics, then the gun may
be selectively positioned in abutment with any patch area of said film in realm
of movement of the apparatus 10. Jerome Lemelson Jan 22, 1960 Lenore Waldmeyer

January 26, 1960 Applications and improvements in TPR (GE. thermoplastic
recording) It is conceived to adapt the recently released T.P.R system to single
frame recording for so called "animated cartooning" or the like. The system as
announced by G.E. involves only the production of motion pictures and since the
section of the thermoplastic tape heated by induction (in the G.E. apparatus) is
well in advance of the section or length of the tape, it is not possible to
shoot individual frames with a time delay between each which is ~~ faster ~~
longer than the time it takes for the frame to pass thru modification to the
apparatus. Accordingly, a number of modifications to apparatus of this type are
hereby proposed to effect "cartooning" or single frame function. (1.) In the
first apparatus, automatic control means are provided for automatically drawing
the single exposed frame~~ pa ~~ of tape pat the induction heating means to form
the so called "ripple" image in the thermoplastic and when so formed (after
the~~ same ~~single frame section has passed the heating device, the induction
heater is automatically turned off, followed by the automatic reversal of the

FIG. 2 In the drawing (at the left,) all stationery components are assembled to
be supported by the walls of the housing 101 or bracket extending thereafter.
The apparatus 100 consists of a sealed enclosure 101 having a gear motor 102
mounted therein for driving a disc 104 which is a multilayer TPR. recording
material produced in accordance with the G. E. TPR tape with the exception that
the high melting base film is rigid enough to maintain the disc in a rigid
planer shape when rotated at recording speed by 102. An electron-gun 106
provides a raster scan or the like on an annular surface of 104 which provides
an annular charge pattern thereon. A first R.F. heater is positioned "down
stream" of 106 which melts the thermoplastic layer of 104 wherein the electro
static charges on the film and the ground plane depress the surface of the
melted layer creating the so called ripple pattern therein. The rippled surface
then ~~ is rotated ~~ passes thru an optical septum 110, 110' which may be used
for the projection of the image onto a screen or to an electronic scanning
device such as a cathode ray reading tube or the like. A second RF heater 112
heats the exposed area to a sufficiently high temperature to "erase" the ripple
pattern before it passes thru the exposure scanning field of 106. Several
variations in the apparatus of Fig. 2 are noted. (a) ~~ If ~~ The apparatus 100,
may be used as a temporary storage device for storing pictorial, analog or
digital information. In this embodiment, the erasure heater 112 may be in
constant operation or may ~~ er ~~ operate only upon command to erase only
predetermined areas of the annular exposure band such as areas containing
information which has been processed, identified or otherwise used. (In this
respect, the erasure heater 30, Fig. 1 p. 72 of the closed loop tape transport
may also be programmed in 1/31/60 LW EW 2/1/60 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ AND

claimed S The panel 10 of Fig. 1 is preferably made by the Tube-In-Strip or Roll
Bond Processes. It consists of an oblong rectangular sheet 11 of ~~Po  aluminum
or other metal having a plurality of vein-like duct portions 12a to 12e
preferably extending most of the length of the sheet and preferably closed at

sealing of the ~~ The duct portions are preferably ~~ forme ~~ formed by the

suitable solid. Such material may be introduced after the duct portions are ~~
allowed to harden ~~ are formed or may be used in its fluid state and under
pressure to inflate the duct formations 12-. Another suitable material is a
framed plastic which is mixed and introduced into the ducts of 12 in its

support for the walls of said vein-like ducts The panel 10 is shown in a simple

~~ 3c. ST Ultrasonic Cleaning Apparatus It has been conceived to clean an
article such as a flexible cloth or any rigid article by subjectin all or part
of said article to ultrasonic Mach waves or shock waves generated in a vapor-gas
mixture surrounding said article whereby molecules of said vapor (steam and/or
cleaning fluid) are caused to impinge against and be removed from said article
by the ultrasonic ~~ de ~~ vibrations or shock waves. In certain cases, the
waves may be used to ~~ m ~~ cause the vapor to better penetrate the surface or
strands (if cloth) of the article. In other cases, the vapor may be made to
penetrate and/or deflect off the article by virtue of its velocity which
impingement may THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY JB DATE 5/9/60
THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY EJW 4/19/60

be effected prior to and/or during the generation of the pressure waves in the
volume surrounding the article. viz. (a) Apparatus and process in which article
is introduced into a chamber having a vapor of a cleaning fluid continuously
introduced and ~~ tube ~~ high frequency and/or intensity ~~ m ~~ pressure waves
generated in said chamber and/or in said vapor and directed against said article
(b) Similar to (a) is which the vapor is directed against the article as a

### Page 97
high velocity jet (from various angles) either continuously or intermittently
and in which the waves ~~ arg ~~ are generated either continuously or
intermittently. (c) Apparatus of (a) in which the article is moved (rotated or
tumbled) ~~ in ~~ as the vapor and pressure waves are generated either
continuously or intermittently. (d) Any of processes (a) to (c) in which a
liquid stream or spray directed against the article supplements or replaces the
vapor. If it replaces, the ultrasonic vibrations in the gas volume around the

The following improvements in articles and materials are conceived: ~~ in which
~~ It is known to improve the physical and chemical characteristics of certain
materials such as plastics by exposure to high energy particles such as X-rays,
atomic radiation, etc. The temperature resistance of certain plastics such as
polyethylenes may be increased by as much as 50% or more, electrical insulation
improved and often physical appearance improved or changed after irradiation
treatment using radioactive materials or high energy generators such as the Van
de Gaff

### Page 103
generator to expose the materials thereto. It is conceived by me to change only
selected areas, portions or parts of articles by radiation of only said areas or
concentration of the radiant energy ~~ only on ~~ on said areas while exposing
other areas to lesser doses. Improved articles are conceived as follows I (a)
Plastic-sheet in which only selected areas thereof have been irradiated (or
concentrated with radiation as compared with lesser exposure for others) to
change strength dielectric constant, heat resistance, rigidity or flexibility,
clarity or color viz: (1) Border areas (bands) of sheet made rigid while center
is more flexible by irradiating only border areas. (2) Spaced parallel band
areas of a sheet irradiated to make them more rigid while areas between are more
flexible (3) Spot or patch areas of same or different designs made more rigid
while areas in between are ~~ flex ~~ more flexible (4) Quilt or cris-cross
(hatched) designs of irradiated areas while areas in between are more flexible
(over) EJW May 8, 1960 THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ & UNDERSTOOD BY JB DATE
5/9/60

### Page 104
These design for a plastic sheet will ~~ form ~~ provide a material which is
flexible and may be used in packaging, yet which has reenforcing bands formed of
more rigid (irradiated) portions of the same material for added strength. Note
A- The plastic sheet may be irradiated as it is extruded, a calandered or while
otherwise in a molted state, by beams of radiant energy directed against the
moving sheet Note B- Irradiation may be effected by using a shield or mask to
prevent irradiation of areas not to be so changed Note C- Irradiation may be
used to change color, clarity or to provide unique designs in band or other
areas of sheet. The mask itself may provide ~~ the ~~ unusual contours in the
plastic sheet if it (a) moves with the sheet (radiator stationery), (b) sheet
and mask are stationery while radiation source irradiates (then turns off or is
shuttered off) Note D: If a mask such as lead is used which varies in thickness
across the mask, then if a constant intensity source of radiation is used the
areas of the sheet or article being irradiated which are in line with the
thinner portions of the mask will receive greater doses of radiation than those
areas in line with heavier portions of the mask. If color changes in the
material are experienced in proportion to the radiation, then shade may be
controlled by mask thickness (as well as radiation intensity and time of
exposure) and different shades of color or clarity may be effected in a design
in the irradiated material by using a mask having certain areas thicker than
others. A mask of tapering thickness will produce a gradual variation in color

May 22, 1960 I Telephone System Computer It has been conceived to design a
scanner and computing device which senses overload or peak loading, on approach
to overload or peak load in a phone switching system and rerouts  calls through
other circuits or switches standby ~~ or ~~ ~~ low ~~ circuits or circuits of
lower loading into system approaching overload. This may be effected by several
manners including the use of a scanning device which constantly scans a number
of representative circuits in a system and notes the rate of change in which
said circuits become operative and inoperative. If a large enough number are
scanned (number determined statistically) it can be ~~ alli ~~ determined ~~ tha
~~ that the switching system is becoming loaded at the same rate and when the
rate approaches or ~~ by ~~ increases beyond a certain value ~~ or value ~~ or
values automatic switching of standby systems into the system in use may be
effected. A computer of this type may also be employed to sense changes in power
demands on a power system such as a public utility electrical power generating
and distributing system whereby additional generators are put into the system to

means for focusing sunlight with a semi-conductor means or other means for
converting heat into electricity to provide an efficient heat-to-electricity
energy converter. Reference is made to a plastic parabolic or spherical
reflector developed by me several months ago and recorded in another notebook
which may be used in one or more of the following configurations: Fig. 1

RECORD OF CONCEPTIONS OF INVENTIONS I Glass Roll-Bond (tube-in-strip) processes
for making neon signs. Several years ago I conceived the idea for providing a
hollow, vein-like duct in a sheet of glass, ceramic or plastic which duct may
contain electrodes and a gas such as argon, neon, etc for use as a neon sign.
Following are conceived manufacturing techniques which I intend to file

### Page 124
patents applications on. (a) Hot roll glass into a sheet, print the desired sign
pattern as a stopweld material while sheet is still hot; roll a second hot sheet
of glass over first sheet fusing or welding those areas between the two not
covered by stop-weld, insert an inflation tool between sheets and inflate the
vein-like area as in Roll-bond (while one or both of the sheet materials is
still semi-molten ~~ and ~~ thereafter ~~ further ~~ allow the sheets to
solidify (while maintaining sufficient air or fluid pressure to prevent
buckling, and further fabricating by inserting electrodes, gas and sealing. (b)
Same as (a) except that stop-weld is applied to a cold or non-molten sheet which
is brought up to desired temperature thereafter by radiant, induction or other
means. (c) At least one of the sheets are hot pressed between dies with the
desired letters in it and is thereafter bonded to a flat sheet (areas between
letters are welded or adhesively bonded to a flat glass or metal sheet and
processed with electrodes, gas, etc (d) Same as (a) but stop weld print is
replaced by a roll-bond tubed sheet or the tubular area of a Roll-bond sheet
with the areas therebetween (tubes) etch away. ~~ Sheet is ~~ Roll-bond tubed
portion is rolled between two sheets of ~~ metal ~~ glass which are fused
together when in their molten state and THIS CONFIDENTIAL MATTER READ &
UNDERSTOOD BY JB DATE 9/15/60

### Page 125
Roll bond metal sheet portion is inflated while glass is still in molten
condition. After glass with R-bond encased therein is cooled an etchant liquid
is flowed into inflated metal strip therein to etch away metal leaving only
glass in the tubular portion of sheet. (e) Same as (d) but Roll Bonded strip is
replaced with a tube of metal bent to desired shape and placed between two glass
sheets which are hot rolled into one sheet encapsulating metal tube therein
which is later etched away. to be continued/ Thermo-plastic Recording It is

multiple of) beam may be automatically controlled in an automatic cycle of
operation by means of a programming means such as a magnetic or other recorder
on which is recorded the necessary analog and/or digital signals to effect such
control which recorder is operated and transduced from to derive said signals in
a predetermined sequence (3) Matereal to be deposited may be admitted to beam as

made. (4) Chemical reactions, alloying, doping, etc. may take place in beam or

5. Machinery or otherwise physically and chemically changing material deposited

5. Machining or otherwise physically and chemically changing material deposited

beams contain atoms of material to be deposited onto surface by main beam which
may be deflection controlled thereafter in accordance with a programmed input.
9. The optical maser may be used as an auxilliary beam generator in conjunction
with above arrangements or in place of electron beams generating means therefor.

Nov. 10, 1948 Records of Inventions: ADJUSTABLE AIR GAGE SPINDLE: Reference:
"Precision Working in The Metal Working Working Industry"Volume Two. Syracuse
University Press. p.p. 146 - 151 The author conceives the need for an adjustable
internal (and external) air gage spindle for use in measuring internal &
external diameters by the use of air flow. This would eliminate the need for a
spindle size for each diameter to be measured. Preliminary Sketch: A- Spindles
B- Air Jet Holes C- Spindle Holder D- Diameter to be meas'd. E- Adjustable
Spindle Braces. F.- Set Screws for braces. G- Airlines to B. (flexible)

Nov. 10-1948 Change in design of spindle A. In order to increase the accuracy of
the instrument and the range of the limits of the indicator, the following
design is considered.

August 19, 1949 - Air Conditioner Work on the following invention which was
conceived by Alan Nathan and myself was begun this week and will continue until
successfully developed. The inventions purpose it to provide a cheap means of
air conditioning for a person or persons sleeping by placing a tent over the bed
and piping in conditioned air which has been processed by a small conditioning
unit. The unit should be able to supply air which has been controlled in
temperature and moisture content. August 18 - Purchased small blower and motor
for construction of small unit mentioned above.

### Page 6
The following figures were obtained from the TRANE Air Conditioning manual
REQUIRED flow of outside Air (Room Air) per person is 5-7.5 cu ft/min. Cooling
load for Ventilating air: DEsign outdoor wet bulb temp is 80 Conditioned space =
68 48.3 BTU/hr. per cfm of outside air. or if 5-7.5 c.fm per person :reg'd
250-375 BTU/hr. per person to be removed. (1) Body heat to be removed (Estmated)
Person at rest= 400 BTU/hr. Mild Exercize- 675 BTU/hr. Heat to be removed from
unit/unit time =(1) Heat transferred thru tent walls/unit time +(2) Heat given
up by body of person. Required- Thermal resistivity of material Sept.27-1949
Continuing with the development of above invention: Thermal resistivity of
vinylite plastic. = .6 BTU~~ / ~~ inches/sq-ft/hr/F.

Lemelson November 2, 1949 Today I conceived several new inventions which will be
developed when possible in the near future: Perhaps the most novel is the
following invention of a X-mas ornament. Ornament with a Blinking Optical
Effect: The ornament consists of a thin walled shell charged with
cyclindrically, spherically, like the frustrum of a cone (to represent the shape
of a X-mas tree), etc. inside of which is mounted a spiraling glass tube, closed
at one end and connected at the other end to the standard 'bubble light'
ornament now on the market. (The 'bubble light' emits gaseous bubbles in liquid
surrounding the light which travel up the glass tube; the gas condensing at the

### Page 10
Nov.2-1949 top of the tube. The inventor has seen the patent on this 'bubble
light' and will look further into this patent in the development of this
invention. As stated, the glass tube winds around the interior of the shell.
Small holes, backed by colored celluloid (or uncovered) are drilled in the shell
opposite the glass tube. The liquid in the tube is opaque so that the bubble,
traveling past the hole has the effect of an opening shutter. Thus as each
bubble passes a hole, a 'blinking on' on the light from the inside of the shell
occurs. Preliminary Sketch of invention:

Spiraling, Twisting or any shape of bubble light rod or tube OPAQUE SHELL OF
ORNAMENT Hole in SHELL Bubble in liquid LIQUID IS OPAQUE STANDARD BUBBLING LIGHT
ORNAMENT BASE

Nov. 2-1949 Other inventions conceived today include Use of almes-magnets (1.) A
cereal or soup bowl with magnets in the bottom to hold it to a metal surface to
prevent spilling. This would be of great use in feeding babies. (2) A drinking
class holder of plastic or other material having magnets in its base to hold it
to a metal surface. This would prevent glass (drinking glass) from tipping when
full. (3) Embedding of magnets in crockery or glass bottoms for the same purpose
mentioned in (2) above, to prevent tipping when full. (4) The use or invention
of magnetic silver ware, knives, forks, etc. for use on metalic topped tables on
airlines, ships, etc. (5) A magnetic tie-clasp utilizing a magnet campled & the
shirt and the clasp, in the form of an ornament, which will be attracted to the
magnet thru tie and hold it in place. Witnessed by: Howard Temekon, Nov. 2, 1949

principle cigarette magnets place in ashtray. (over) Note: Metalic Magnetic
Cigarette Holder: This invention is a device (magnetic) for the purpose of

### Page 15
Nov 6, 1949 the usual placement ~~ of a cigarette ~~ is difficult such as in a
moving automobile where the vibration may jar it loose if just placed in the
ordinary holder. The clamping of the cigarette is accomplished by a light
magnetic force, not enough to squeeze the cigarette so that it is damaged. The
device is so made that the jaws which hold the cigarette do not completely close
when the cigarette is in place. A light magnetic force thus holds the cigarette
in position and removal is relatively easy. Exact design details will be worked
out. Magnetic gears on Magnetic Coupling: A coupling device consisting of two
wheels with teeth of magnetic material is conceived. The teeth do not mesh. One
wheel is turned by the repulsion of the others magnets. Diagram:

Nov. 9, 1949 Today devoted three hours to development of magnetic cigarette
holder and one hour to development of fountain tooth brush. Conception of an
idea for a Toy: The toy consists of two figures free to swivel about their bases
each of which is magnetic. Thus, rotation of one automatically rotates the other
by the repelling action of the magnets in the base. (i.e- all south poles point
out in one figure whereas all north poles point out in the other) Sketch of Toy:
Rotation of one produces rotation in other one DANCING FIGURES Note- figures do
not necessarily have to be attached to base. May be made to spin on table
topJerome Lemelson Nov 9. 1949 Howard Lemelson Nov. 20, 49

November 17, 1949 Today purchased an additional 2.35 worth of magnets plust two
2.25 plastic bits. Continuing with an invention conceived several days prior to
this writing. The invention consists of magnets embedded in plastic discs or
pinned darts which are tossed at a verticle iron or steel target. The inventor
conceives of the same principle applied to a game of skill in which pellets are
magnetized and fired from a target gun at a target of magnetic attracting
material. Toss Game discs:

disk metallic target slightly off verticle magnet Jerome Lemelson magnetic
pellet target Nov. 20, 1949 Conception of Magnetic Game of Skill: called
Obstacle Course. or Pilot.

Nov. 20-49 21 Description of Game: Game consists of playing board of
non-magnetic material which is flat and smooth ~~ f ~~ enough for a small flat
bottomed object to roll or slide over. To this board are attached a number of
magnets, each of which represents an obstacle to the scoring puck or pellet. A
permanent magnet attached to a string, stick or other object or held in the hand
is used as the motivating medium for the puck. This is accomplished by moving it
over the puck which is also a magnet or of magnetic material and allowing the
force of the magnet to slide or roll the puck without lifting it to it. On
scoring, obstacles (magnets) nearest the starting point are scored lowest; when
and if the ultimate goal is reached without attraction to any of the obstacle
magnets, it is scored highest. Attraction to the motivating magnet automatically
eliminates the piece. Diagram of game board:

Motivating stick

### Page 17
Magnet non mag obstacles magnets puck non magnetic obstacles Jerome Lemelson
Witnessed by Howard Lemelson Nov 20, '49

Nov. 21, 1949 Magnetic Game (continued) a variation of the game described on
page 21 would involve the use of a score board without obstacles but with just a
scored path painted on its surface over which the puck must be moved. Segaments
of the path are scored with increasingly higher numbers as the objective or
finishing point are approached. In testing out the magnetic game idea the
inventor noticed that it takes a considerable amount of skill to move the puck
without attracting it to the motivating magnet. The correct distance between the
pucks & motivator must be kept so that it is just lifted off the surface and may
be moved in the desired direction. Variations in game design: 1. The puck may be
shaped like an airplane which must overcome the obstacles along the course. 2.
Magnetic Football Game: The puck may be the ball carrier and the opposite side
composed of movable magnetics which are positioned before hand by the opposite
player. The controller of the puck must move it through the opposition. Jerome
Lemelson Nov. 24, '49

Nov.23,1949 An investigation has been made to "determine the availability of"
magnetic plastics for the above toy. It appears as if very little development
work has been done on magnetic plastics to date with the only available shapes
on the

market today being cylinders which are used for electronic work. Until such is
developed in sheet form for this toy, the inventor suggests the following
construction for the toy described on pp. 23,24 Backboard The assembly board on
which the shapes are mounted is made of sheet steel or iron or other magnetic
material (not a magnet) Assembly pieces: Piece #1, the head of the figure, is
made of a piece of sheet metal which is magnetic attractive. Set in the piece or
glued to it are small flat magnets for attraction to the backboard. The other
pieces 2,3,4,5,6,7,8, etc. are made of colored sheet plastic with small flat
magnets set in them for attachment to the backboard or glued to them. Typical

magnet Nov.26,1949 Referring to the invention described on pp. 9 and 10 in this
note book (a chemically

### Page 21
Nov. 26,1949 heated shoe), the inventor some time ago conceived of the following
method of shoe heating. The device ~~ of ~~ consists of a specially constructed
shoe which is insulated beneath the second sole, the second sole and heel made
with hollow cavities into which may be placed a cartridge or several cartridges
which, in turn, contain the reacting chemicals previously described. The
chemicals are separated from each other and may be caused to mix by bending the
cartridge or by some other mechanical manipulation such as the pressure of the
foot squeezing it. The inventor further recommends the uses of two chemicals
such as those used in the Thermite welding process, (iron oxide and aluminum)
which, as it is understood at this reading, is used in portable soldering irons
today to generate heat. Information on the  so called 'heat capsules' has been
requested from the manufacturer, a firm in Maryland. The inventor wishes to
bring out the following points on this invention. (1) The use of a highly
conductive witnessed by H. Lemelson Nov. 27, 1949 Nov. 26, 1949 material which
surrounds the capsule (heating capsule) cavity or heating tubes if a liquid
mixture of exothermic chemicals is added thru the valves (see p. 10) and which
extends to the far sections of the sole in contact with the foot of the wearer
for the conduction of heat to all the parts of the sole. (2) Design of the
Capsule: Due to the tremendous heat liberated when the Thermite process occurs,
it may be necessary to place the chemicals between two sheets of metal which are
placed close together; thus limiting the time of reaction. It is obvious to the
inventor that a method is needed for the regulation of the process such as a
valving system which allows only a small amount of the chemicals to react at a
time. (3)If exothermic liquids are used they may be introduced into a flat steel
walled cavity or tank which is embedded in the sole rather than the tubing
described. This would allow an easy replacement of the container if it is made
to slip out from the cavity in which it fits. Filling would be simplest thru one
way valves from a pressurized container. Jerome Lemelson Nov. 26-1949 Witnessed
by H. Lemelen, Nov. 27, 1949

Kine-mag: The name "kin-e-mag" is hereby formally recorded as a name to be
applied to the following magnetic toy and educational game. The toy is similar
in principle to the one described above, the variation being that the
controlling mechanism below the board consists of adjustable linkages,

slides and rotating arms so that magnets traveling below the surface can be
adjusted to travel a number of different shaped paths. The mechanism is motor
driven and easily accessible so that variations in the linkages may be made by
the operator when desired. Simple kimematies is thus taught to the youngster who
is mechanically minded. Adjustments in linkage arms, etc. may be easily made by
tightening and loosening small wing nuts or screws with a screw driver. The
kenematic mechanism may consist of, (1) Fixed posts (guides) for split arms or
sliding guides which may be positioned in a groove beneath the surface by the
lightening of a wingnut. (2) split arms and (or) rod slides ( a arm hinges on
here;

To be worked out after consulting a kenematics book: Jerome Lamelson Witnessed

apple may be made to move up and

### Page 25
down as does a humans in swallowing by placing a round weight or ball in the

curl up as in a smile or the eyes to open wide by linkages. Relatively flexible
rubber would be needed to imitate the facial and neck skin of the down. The
weight or ball would be recovered from the back of the doll. The same principle
could be applied to a small hard banks doll which smiles when a coin is
deposited in its mouth or thru  a slot in its head. Witnessed by: H. Lemelov
11/29/49 II  Haircutting Doll: (1) This doll has a portion of its upper skull
removable under which a loose wig (of grass etc) may be placed, there being hair
on the repacible. Thus a wig may be positioned by the child and trimmed with a
scissor. The child thus imitates a barber. (2) The same effect may be

placed and grass or chard is grown. The doll could be a window sill ornament for
the child to trim:every now and then. Witnessed by H. Lemelov 11/29/49 III
Hatching Chick Toy: This toy consists of an imitation egg shell (of plastic or
some other similar material) inside of which is a tiny chick. The egg is
assembled from two parts which realistically crack apart when a toy hen is
placed on it. This is accomplished as follows. The egg made ~~ to ~~ of two
separate partitions snaps together by a latch on the inside of the egg. A hole
through the shell to the latch is a recepticle ~~ to the latch ~~ for a peg in
the bottom of the hen. Thus when the peg is put in the hole and the peg is faced
down, the egg splits in two. The ~~latch ~~ egg may be spring loaded so that
once it is forced by the peg, there is a force alerted to open the shell.
Diagram: (spring loaded Latch) - crack in shell - Peg - Hole spring loaded latch
- Chick - egg shell - Spring loaded hinge tending to force egg apart.

Pivot squirrel to deposit nuts in various holes, Depending on ball Operation of
this toy is as follows: A toy squirrel (6) pivots about its base which is hinged

attained. Round steel balls representing nuts are placed in a nest(2) which is

down the hollow branch into the paw on outstretched

Nov.28-1949 arms of the squirrel(6) thus upsetting the balance. The squirrel
then tips, depositing the ball in a hole in the base of the tree (9) and it
rolls behind the tree into a container (8). To regulate the flow of the balls so
that ~~the return of~~ all the balls do not flow at once, the return of his paw
may trip a lever which allows another ball to roll down. Jerome Temelson

Witnessed by H. Lemelson 11/29/49 Nov.29, 1949 Conception of Several New Toy
Inventions: (I.) Magnetic Trapese Artists Toy: This invention utilizes the
phenomena of magnetic attraction and the fact that a magnet may be uncoupled
from a piece of iron or another magnet by a light force depending on the
strength of the magnet. The toy consists of a miniature replica of the circus
trapese artists. A small light toy figure of the performer is suspended from one
of the trapeses bars by a magnet in its base. The figure is cast outstretched ~~
and ~~ and ~~ if ~~ reaching out with its arms or, it may have movable legs and
arms for variation by the player. The hands of the figure are hook shaped so
that they may hook over the other bar or a bar suspended from another figure. (A
multitude of variations are possible. NOTE: An electromagnet on each bar, which
may be turned on and off, may be used rather than permanent magnets.) The toy
game or toy may be played in

Nov.29, 1949 several ways. Both the figure and the receiving trapese may be set
in motion by release from a high point on the usual ~~ as ~~ starting point of
circus performers by the use of a release latch or they may simply be put in
motion by the hand. Pressing a button may shut off the electromagnet ~~ at ~~ on
the bar of the toy performer and release him to the other bar or his hooking to
the other bar may separate his permanent magnetic base from the original bar.
Two performers may also be used using magnets of different strength so that one
may be uncoupled while the other holds fast. The hooking action may be attained
by an outstretched bar attached to the hands of one performer. Again, the
release of one figure may be accomplished by an electromagnet shutting off on
the bar to which he is attracted or by hooking to the other bar. Sketch:

Jerome Lemelson Nov. 29-1949

### Page 31
Note: In respect to the trapese toy, coupling of the two figure may be

Lemelson 11/29/49 II. Propelled Toy Ducks: or Whate (WHALE). This invention
consists of a toy duck OR WHALE of light ~~ colored ~~ material such as plastic;
wood, rubber etc a light metal which floats stabely and is propelled thru the
water in one of the following manners. I. Mechanical Propulsion: This may be
attained thru a paddle coupled to a winding spring or a paddle wheel also spring
wound, on by a propeller coupled to a winding spring. II. Jet Propulsion: This
may be accomplished in one of several ways. (a) By steam pressure utilizing a
standard put-put system in which a small candle or tablet is burned under a
small tank of water. A pressure is thus built up against the back pressure of
the water, the steam being emitted at rapid intervals causing a net forward
thrust - (known to the art) (b) By the inflation of a plastic bag

Nov. 29, 1949 or baloon within the toy figure and the resulting escape of the
gases rearward A simple baloon may be used which inflates within the figure to
its approximate shape or the following system may be employed The inside baloon
~~ figure ~~ may be blown up at some point on figure's surface such as the bill
of the duck, the spout point of the whale, etc. A one way valve consisting of a
tiny ball and seat at the filling joint may be utilized to prevent escape from
this point. During filling, the escape nozzle may be shut off by a twisting
action or by a plug. This too may have a one way (escape) action to prevent
water from filling the figures bladder: A small spring loaded ball would suffice
for this purpose. The same principle may be applies to the other shapes of the
toys. Jerome Lemelson Witnessed by: H Lemelson 11/29/49 (Refer to pp. 11-13) The

Nov. 30, 1949 Conception of Inventions: I. Toy Cow Which Can Be Milked: This toy
consists of the figure of a cow which is molded, stamped, or otherwise formed of
a light material and which has the following mechanism so that the cow may be
milked. The cows head may be manufactured so that it is bending over, or may be
made to bend over a pan containing milk, water, or other liquid which resembles
milk. A tube in the cows mouth submerges in the liquid with the mouth. The cow
drinks up the liquid when to operator pumps the tail or pulls it, thus either
operating a pump in the body of the cow or drawing in on a piston and filling in
the manner that a syringe is filled. The piston is spring loaded so that the
liquid is under pressure. A one way valve at the mouth prevents the liquid from
flowing out the mouth. A valve at the cows ~~ brest ~~ breast is made so that
it will allow passage of the fluid only when the breast is pulled as in milking
the real cow. The cow can be made to moo when its milked for realism. A
preliminary sketch will be drawn when the inventor finds time in a few days.
(over)

November 30, 1949 Spouting Wale (Propelled) This toy consists of a floating
replica of a wall of light material inside of which is a mechanism for loading
(filling a reservoir with water") similar to that in the cow. Intake is through
an opening or hole in the bottom of the whale (a one way valve consisting
possibly of a spring-loaded ball and seat preventing outflow thru the intake. A
string, lever (pull type) or pumping tail or fin loads the water reservoir which
is spring-loaded for pressurization and loaded by a piston. ~~This so ~~ Outflow
of the water is used for two purposes, (1) to create a spout characteristic of
the whale (water spout) and (2) to flow rearward out the tail and of the ~~ whel
~~ and propell the whale throu the water. This toy will be sketched in detail at
the inventors first opportunity. The drawings of all the inventions in this

Record of Conception of New Inventions The following inventions were conceived
on this date all involving the spring

### Page 35
Dec. 1-49 loaded piston described in the inventions on the preceding two pages.
The spring loaded piston is used as a source of energy to supply a stream of
water for an optical effect or may be used to propell a device (toy) thru the
water. The following sketch will describe it for a preliminary design
considerations. (large intake valve opening for easy loading) 1) is a pull rod
for loading or cocking the piston. It is pulled back by the operator in loading:
(2) is a spring which is compressed when the piston is cocked. (3) is the
cylinder or shell in which the piston slides,(4), the piston, (5) the reservoir
for the liquid, (6) may be a one way intake valve and (7) a one way exhaust
valve which may be shut on or off for loading by a screw, needle valve, etc. The
device is being developed by the inventor. Jet Propelled Boat: This toy consists
of a toy boat made of a light or hollow material inside of which is placed the
above spring loaded piston. The piston is cocked directly by hand

Dec. 1,1949 possibly by the use of a lever to gain a mechanical advantage. To
minimize leaks, it should be made of a relatively flexible or soft material
which expands when wet against the walls of the cylinder. It should be backed
with a stiff material - Rubber may serve the purpose of the flexible material
Diagram:

II JET VALVE CONTROL InTake & valve Piston STRong Spring. loading Arm. (or a
string may be attached to the piston rod here and pulled) Cocking the piston
loads the reservoir. When released, the spring forces the piston rearward and
since water is an incompressible liquid, the pressure of the spring forces it
out of the exhaust orifice at a high velocity which jet propells the boat. III
Fire Boat: Note: an additional tap off hose or line may be run from the cylinder
to supply water for a fire hose treated on the deck of the boat. IV Paint
Sprayer: The spring loaded piston and cylinder may also be utilized for spraying
small quantities at a time of thin paint. This could be utilized for a cheap
sprayer for such items a touch up

paint for automobiles, window cleanser fluid, liquid wax, D.D.T. and
insecticide, etc. to be expanded. V Toy Game: This game consists of a statically
mounted on moving toy figure which is composed of parts which ~~are~~
magnetically hold each other together. The object of the game is to knock the
figure apart with pellets from a spring loaded gun. For example, the figure may
be that of a snowman of white plastic. The pellets may be shaped & colored like
snowballs. The idea or purpose would be to attempt of break-up the snowman by
first hitting this to magnetically held on hat, then his head then his limbs,
etc. To be expanded. VI. Toy Automobile which can be stopped at red light. This
toy consists of a small wind up or battery powered automobile which turns around
on a smooth ~~back~~ forward on a table. A traffic light at one point of the
roadbed or track can be operated on or off, red or green. When the red is
operated, an electric magnet beneath the roadbed is turned on, and this in turn
causes Dec. 1, 1949 the toy to stop by either attracting a light spring loaded
switch in the car cutting off its powder (under the body of the car) or just
holding the car to the board. The car would have to have its body's bottom
nearly sliding on the surface for this latter technique to succeed. The author
has just conceived of further applications of this principle. The
electro-magnets placed at various points under the roadbed may be made to cause
the toy to go thru various gyrations, and to control its motion by holding
itself and necessarily the car perhaps say 90 degrees to its original direction
~~with~~ by using another electro magnet for rotation. A small alnico permanent
magnet in the car may help the action. Further investigation and development is
necessary. Jerome Lemelson Dec. 1, 1949 Witnessed by H. Lemelson Dec. 5, 1949

5, 1949 Doll With a Heart Beat This invention involves the placing of a single
spring wound mechanism with an endurance of several minutes or more inside

the doll or puppet. The noise of the heart beat may be attained in one of
several ~~ a number of ways namely: (1) By having a light arm, attached to the
mechanism, strike a hollow drum or sounding board at a pace similar to normal
heartbeat. (2) By the use of a watch or clock mechanism of correct dimensions
and material to produce a beat which is somewhat like a heartbeat. (3) By the
use of a small electric motor coupled to the correct mechanism for the
production of a beat. (4) By the use of an electro-vibrator of a slow frequency
(80 to 100 per second) which flexes a membrane or drum. Others will be recorded
as conceived. Manicuring Doll: This invention refers to a toy figure or doll
which can be manicured by the playing child. This is accomplished by the use of
plastic finger nails which are removable and replaceable merely by snapping them
into the finger roots. They are held in place by compression of the plastic
finger nail as it is bent for inserted into The toy is unique in that the nails

Dec. 4, 1949 A conventional doll's head is so made that a small hole (1) is
formed in the middle of its lips which connects to tubing (3). The hole may be
so tapered that insertion of the tube to the end of a conventional or especially
made whistle for the doll may fit in and be held securely by a little pressure.
A tapered hole for example would suffice. The tubing (3) may either extend out
the back of the doll so that the whistle may be blown by a human; may extend to
a bellows in the doll so that squeezing will blow the whistle or may extend to a
bellows outside the doll which may be squeezed. Drinking Doll: This refers to a
doll which drinks water or other liquid thru a straw. The straw again fits in a
small tapered hole in the doll's lips. The liquid is conducted thru a tube in
the body of the doll to a diaper exit as in the well known diaper Dy-Dee doll.
Suction may be attained in one of the several ways. The well known suction pump
which connects to a water supply (running) may be employed (utilizing the
Bernoulli principle of pressure drop at the down stream end.).

### Page 40
The syphon phenomenon may be employed

### Page 41
Dec. 4, 1949 with the source of liquid higher than the exit or down stream end
of the interval tubing in the doll. A flexible tubing straw would probably be
needed to simplify the syphon action. A small pump operated by a spring wound
motor may also be employed. A spring loaded suction piston or diaphram may be
employed (see pp. 50, 54). The piston would be so arranged that the liquid would
be drawn by the piston ~~ rather th ~~ into the cylinder rather than forced out.

Dec. 5, 1949 Variations of the Bubble Light(opaque) Applications:

I. Opaque bubble light placed in front of slot in shell. This application
   produces the effect so that the bubbles themselves will be seen to rise while
   the rest of the opaque liquid keeps out the light behind or inside of the
   ornamental shell. The following sketch will help to clarify:

Viewer I Viewer

The observer at (1) looks at slot (6) in container (3) inside of which are
mounted my opaque bubble lights each effectively covering a slot such as (6).
The opaque liquid in the bubble light (2) is thus viewed thru the slot. A light
bulb (5) supplies the light which penetrate thru the bubbles as they ascend. The
inventor wishes to make it clear

### Page 45
Dec.5.49 that there are numerous variations in the application of this principle
One application involves placing the bubble lamps ~~ in ~~ behind slots in a
shell which is placed in a glass to represent the liquid efforvesing or bubbling
such as in a glass of CocaCola, etc. Of the outer display glass is translucent
and colored a dark brown or other color, the effect of the traveling bubbles in
the opaque liquid and permitting light to pass thru them as they ascend is like
the bubbling in a glass of cola or other carbonated drink. The invention can
thus be applied to any toy or small display advertizing unit which requires a
cheap method of blinking tiny lights on and off or a rising light bounce for
optical effect such as bubbles in a liquid, etc. A miniature toy such as the
movie house with twinkling or blinking lights described on page 14 will now be
expanded a bit upon. The sketch on page 67., (1) represents a toy frame of a
theater made of plastic; wood, metal sheet or other light material (2)
represents its sign which is made to resemble the blinking sign of the average

movie theater by application of the opaque bubble light and hole or slot effect.
The effect of a row of light blinking on and off may be attained by placing a
series of small holes in a row at close intervals to each other. The holes (3)
in the sign (2) are shown. A plug 6, is attached to an extention coard (5) which
in turn receives the bubble light plug (7) (4). Sketch.

December 7, 1949 Conception of Invention: The following invention applying the
bubble tube described at the bottom of page (68) to an article of clothing such
as a ~~ smal boys skull cap or other hat is conceived. Sketch:

A standard heat type bubble tube which will react to the warmth of the human
body. An experiment consisting of a bubble tube (1), an expansion chamber (2), a
restricted or necked down section (3) and the low vapor pressure liquid (6) is
sewn into the top of a boys cap or hat (5). (4) Signifies material used to hold
the chamber (2) and tube in place. An experiment by the inventor has shown that
the heat given off from the human head thru the hair and also thru a piece of
cloth is sufficient to start and

Dec. 7, 1949 maintain the bubble effect. Thus the wearer of the cap has a device
which continually bubbles while he is wearing it. The device w ~~ device and cap
will be further developed. Jerome Lemelson Dec. 7, 1949 Witnessed by: H.

January 2, 1950 Nine hours of experimentation today with the bubble tube
described on pp - 12, 60 - 69, 70 and 71 involved the use of a vacuum pump, a,
Tconnection with shut off valves, CC14, and necessary glass tubing and working
tools. Several tubes containing CC14 as the bubbling liquid were made to operate
successfully by heat from the hand. It was discovered that the beck down section
in the bubble tube (restriction, re: pp. 68-72) can connect to a section which
is in line with the bubble tube provided that the restriction is the right
diameter. Diagram : B - Tube; Bubbles in Liquid; A - Restriction; C Chamber.
This operates quite satisfactory, particularly if the heat is applied to A. The
bubbles are large and numerous if the Chamber C is just brought in contact with
an electric bulb or placed above the bulb. The heat of the hand will also work
quite well. With this knowledge, the inventor has conceived of the following
construction for a bubble cap device first described on pp. 70 and 71 Referring

H-Lemelson 5, Jan 3, 1950 Since a black (opaque) liquid in the heavier (larger
diameter) tube may prevent the transmittal of light due to the liquid flowing
down the side of the tube, the following tubing construction is conceived as a
poseable solution to the problem. Crosssectional views of :

The shaded areas (1),(2) and (3) refer to small channels in the tubing thru
which the opaque liquid may flow as the buble rises thus permitting the entire
area (x) to be clear to allow light to pass thru tube. Of the tube is titled a
off horizontal, the device will work even better. Titling ordinary round tubing
(with opaque liquid bubbling) alows a clear bubble to flow with the liquid
passing down the side tilted. Jerome Lemelson Jan . 3 - 1950 Witnessed Jan 5,

light, a bubble tube (5) with light impermeable liquid (6) in which is generated
large bubbles (7) light from within ~~ being ~~ traveling thru said bubbles as
they pass openings (8) representing eyes (9) or buttons of the figure. These
blink on and off as the bubbles are generated. See sketch on next page.
Modifications of this design would include glass or plastic rods extending from
the bubble tube to the buttons to conduct the light. Jerome Lemelson Witnessed
by Howard Lemelson 2/28/50

March 9, 1950 Experiments With Nylon Coated Plastics: Experiments ~~ have been
~~, conducted over the past few weeks aimed at curing a low cost plastic so that
it will not be attached by such chemicals as are used in the bubbling devices
described previously in this notebook have terminated this evening with a series
of containers of acetate, and other plastic being successfully coated with a
thin layer of Nylon. This involves the use of Durey cement as a bonding agent on
which liquid Nylon is sprayed. Experiments will continue in testing this
coating. Jerome Lemelson Mar. 9, 1950 Witnessed by Howard Lemelson Mar. 10, 1950
March 13, 1950 Conception of Invention: Title: Compact Plastic Processing Unit
Uses: For filling life rafts and the like with spongy plastic to make it non
sinkable and puncture proof. also for use camping equipment such a tent and hut
flooring, insulation etc This invention is conceived with light spongy plastics
such as Lockfoam (Lockheed Aircraft), stearofoam, etc which are used for
insulation; etc. and particularly those which ~~ are processed ~~ require heat
for processing. The author has conceived of a method and device for making this
plastic in an emergency or Witnessed by Howard Lemelson April 16, 1950

### Page 63
March 13, 1950 when needed for use in the field. Plastics such as Lockfoam, for
example, are first mixed and available in liquid form. When heated (exact
temperatures vary with plastic) they expand to as much as 25 or more times their
original volume and are composed of a cellular structure in which air is trapped
thus making a fine insulating material or filler for life preservers, life
boats, etc. The following sketch is a preliminary design of a compact unit for
the production of this plastic in its expanded form so that it may be made
easily outside of the laboratory or factory with a minimum of effort.

For a description of the unit I refer to the above sketch. The unit is housed in
Witnessed by H. Lemelson April 16, 1950

March 13, 1950 a container (1) which is shown in crossection. The container
contains an inner container (2). Which is surrounded by a chemical or chemicals
(3) for the production of an exotheric reaction. If thermite or similar
chemicals are used, an igniter (5) may be utilized to start the exothermic
reactions to produce heat. If two reacting chemicals are utilized they may be
kept apart be partitions or separate containers. In this latter case, their
bringlong together by breaking the partition or one of the containers may be
accomplished by a hammer tap or other means which may be manually done or
automatically through a mechanism. Once heat is generated around container (2),
stopper may either melt or be forced out by the pressure within (2) as the
plastic expands, thus filling whatever space is desired. One or more of these
units may be placed in a deflated life raft for example. When it is desired to
inflate the raft (in an emergency for example) a C02 cartridge may be triggered,
the same action triggering this unit for the production of the plastic which
fills the raft thus making it punctureproof (over) Witnessed by Howard Lemelson
April 16, 1950

### Page 64
March 13, 1950 Another use may be in a compact artic tent where insulation is
needed for the flooring. In this case, the unit would be placed in a deflated
bag for use when needed. The unit may also be used for wall insulation in homes,
etc, for toys wherein it fills a baloon to make a permanent toy baloon shape. To
be further investigated Jerome Lemelson March 13, 1950 April 16, 1950 Note: The
interval between Mar. 13 and Apr. 16 during which time no entries were made in
this book was due to (1) the inventor studying for examinations, (2) magazine
article committments and (3) a 10 day vacation. The following devices were
conceived during the aforementioned interval and are recorded now for the first
time. #1 Tire Handling Device: This device is intended to be used to simplify
the changing of tires by the car operator when a flat tire occurs on the road.
It provides (a) a means for handling the spare and blown out tire with minimum
effort and lessened Witnessed by: H. Lemelson April 16, 1950

chance or dirtying hands and clothing and (2) a means for positioning the tire
prior to placing it on the wheel hub. A sketch will suffice:

The device consists of a frame of steel tubing which fits around the auto wheel,
said wheel resting on spindle (1) which goes thru center hole in tire hub. The
frame consists of bars (5) and (4) which are joined at 6 so that they may freely
rotate with respect to each other (2) is a pivoting support bar which supports
(4) thus holding the tire off the ground while it is being prepositioned before
the ~~ wheel ~~ axle hub. Lateral tipping is prevented by a bend (7) in (5)
which rests on the ground. The tire may be pulled up off the ground by handle
(8). A screw in 5 at the bend (7) threads into bolt (3) end when Witnessed by:
Howard Lemelson April 16, 1950

### Page 65
April 16 1950 it is desired to more the tire over the ground by use of the
frame. #2. Automatic Car Jack: This device is a small portable car jack of the
type utilized to change tires and utilizes the pressure stored in a small
cartridge (such as a CO2 cartridge) to do work on a piston and hence raise the
jack and the car. This would require (1) a cartridge contain gas at sufficient
pressure to do the required amount of work (2) A piston (sealed) on which the
gas (expanding) can work (3) a valve for regulating the flow of gas into the
cylinder containing the piston (4) Possibly a means for creating the proper
mechanical advantage necessary (possibly two pistons) (5) a means for releasing
said pressure after the job is done so as to lower the bumper slowly, (6) a
means for allowing the gas in the cartridge to escape and flow thru the system
so as to do work on the piston (7) a safety one way regulator in the event of a
leak in the system. To be continued #3 Device (Machine) for Manufacturing bubble
tubes: The inventor has conceived of a new technique for mass producing bubble
tubes, Witnessed by: Howard Lemelson April 16, 1950

April 16, 1950 particularly in the manufacture of tubes of plastic material.
However, the method may also be utilized for glass tube manufacture. The
following is a simple sketch of the basic elements involved:

(1) Refers to the walls of the container or tube which is filled with the liquid
(2) of high vapor pressure low boiling temp. An injection nozzle (3) has a ring
(4) or neopreen or other flexible material which is not affected by the liquid
(2), (4) fitting snugly in a groove in (3) as shown and having an outer diameter
greater than the inner diameter (9) of the tube or container. A hole (6) is
drilled near the perimeter of the tube (6) which exits at (7) and is used to
allow trapped air and liquid to escape from (1) This hole is closed off at (7)
at the proper instant by a stop such as the slide valve arrangement (5) shown.
Action is as follows. Liquid (2) is placed in said tube or container (1) so that
is nearly filled. witnessed by H. Lemelson April 16, 1950

### Page 66
April 16-1950 (3) is then inserted on ring(4) is compressed so as to make a
tight seal in (1). The Tube(3) is then pushed forward until liquid begins to
flow thru(6). This hole (6) is then stopped up at(7) by slide valve(5). The
tube(3) is then drawn out a short distance so that a partial vacuum space
appears somewhere in (1). A liquid material is next injected thru hole(8) and it
solidifies, sealing off(1) from the atmosphere(3) is withdrawn after (10)
solidified sufficiently. Jerome Lemelson April 16-1950 Witnessed by: Howard
Lemelson April 16, 1950 Note: Showed sketch of invention on page 88 (toy

March 22-50 Conception of Device For Cooling Flash bulbs which are used for
internal photography (within the human body): The inventor has been informed
that present methods of photographing the inside of a person prior to operating
involved the use of a flash bulb which must be intense in light energy for a
least 1/25th of a second. With the present technique the patient may receive an
internal burn which may be painful and harmful to him. The author has conceived
of the following method of cooling said bulb after it has flashed for the
photograph. The inventor wished to discipate the heat generated (most of it) by
setting up an endothermic reaction immediately after the bulb has fired and
positioned so as to the discipate most of the heat before harm is done to the
patient. Sketch of invention (preliminary design sketch)

Referring to the above skech which is a basic or primary description of the
components,

### Page 68
May 22, 1950 the light bulb (flash bulb) is connected by wires 7 to an source of
energy and switch outside the body of the patient and is encased in transparent
vial 8 so that light may penetrate (when the bulb is fired) to the ~~ various ~~
desired area. At the same instant the bulb is fired, a valve (2) is opened
allowing a fluid in chamber ~~ one ~~ (1) to enter chamber 3. A quick flow into
chamber 3 may be had by use of a liquid 9 such as Freon or other liquid with a
high vapor pressure. At the same time, valve 4 opens allowing chemical in
chamber 6 to react with liquid in chamber 3 (from chamber 1) said  reaction
being endothermic and of sufficient degree to permit discipation of heat from
bulb (5). Another possible arrangement of this device

(1) refers to chamber filled with one ~~ endothermic ~~ chemical which reacts in
chamber 8 with other chemical from chamber (2) when valve 3 is opened thus
discipating heat from bulb 5 when fired - Valve 3 may be operated by small
solenoid J. Lemelson witness H. Lemelson May 22, 1950

with a welding metal exothermically so as to melt said metal, at the same time
heating up the part to be welded to a sufficient temperature to allow
spotwelding of the parts, said exothermic reaction triggered by a firing pin
which sets off a fuse, said cartridge being displaced and fired by said gun;
said cartridge being held near the point of application by a clamp or jaws which
are part of said gun and made of a material such as a ceramic or other material
which will not fuse with said cartridge when it is reacting. The exothermic
reaction may  be  consist of chemicals such as  and other materials if

ago the author conceived of the following invention and he is now running tests
on some. If a material which is not soluble in water such as cellulose acetate,
pt nitrate, vinylite, paints, etc. is placed (bonded) to a bar of soap and the
soap used, the effect will be to prevent the soap from

### Page 75
Soap:  Sept. 1, 1950 dissolving directly below the material For example, the
author has painted a strip of cellulose acetate ~~ d ~~ on a flat surface of a
bar of soap. After using the soap for a while, it wore away except under the
painted strip leaving a ridge. The following applications are thus possible: (1)
Printing of letters or designs on bar soap in colored or clear plastic or other
non-soluble (water) material for decorative purposes and for advertizing the
brand name of the soap. The lettering and designs will remain and become more
bold as the soap is used (2) Protecting engravings in the soap by coating with a
wear plastic. (3) Shaping the soap (as it is used) by printing or applying
plastics or other non-soluble material. For example - if lateral shaping, strips
are ~~ sh ~~ painted on a bar of soap, after a certain amount of use. Lateral
ridges will be formed making the bar slipproof and easier to handle. Jerome
Lemelson Sept. 1, 1950 Witnessed by: Howard Lemelson, Sept. 4, 1950
