frequency. Fuel System: The standard dyna-jet head and fuel metering jet will be
employed for fuel and air feed. The primary combustion region or chamber is so
designed that head and grid may be moved in respect to each other by screwing
them into the combustion chamber thus varying chamber volume.

Dyna-jet Insert:

Dec. 16-1948

The following design was constructed to be fitted into a standard Dynajet engine
for test runs of the grid in the Dyna-jet engine.

Dyna-Jet Head Insert (stainless steel) Spark Plug grid combustion Chamber TESTS
on jet with above insert: Run: Dec. 17 to Jan. 4-1948 Results: (1) INSERT ~~ Pl
~~ without grid: Engine ~~ tested run ~~ with insert at varying degrees within
jet chamber, failed to run. Insert Modified: walls cut down to minimum; engine
finally resonated at usual dyna-jet length. However, internal threads of insert
were /cut out necessitating new mounting of grid.

Modified Grid Mounting:

JET HEAD grid Bolt (Threaded) Positioning Nuts INSERT DEC. 28-1948 thru Jan. 19,
1949 TimE consumEd in manufacture of an equation timing device consisting of a
d.c. motor and automobile distributor. TESTS will be conducted on the Mark II
with grid and Dyna-jet with grid using this timed equation. DEC. 26-1949 The
Marb II with tailpipe section (6) 24 inches long resonated freely without
compressed air and equation (grid was in place). Attempts to

### Page 8
resonate the engine without the grid met with no success.

Feb. 8- 1949 Mark II design: Distance from head to end of tailpipe = 33" Engine
resonates freely with and without grid (cast iron grid). Grid open area to total
area. = .2 Tot. Lenght: 33", Combust. Chamber length= Grid jet- Thrust= 2# Pulse
jet without grid- 2# Feb 9- 1949 Total length of 2 1/2" i.d. pipe= 33" Thrist
with  - jet head (no grind)= 2# approx. Thrust with grid 3" behind heal= 2#
Note: No appreciable difference was noted in the thrust between  both  grid and
pulse jet engines. Feb. 10, 1949 Grid distance behind head varied 1", 1 1/2",
2". No apparent increase in thrust.

Feb. 16, Grid Area Reduced 17x (.20)^2

Feb. 18, Attempts were made to force resonate the jet at double its natural
frequency. The apparatus broke down at l a rotor speed of 3200 r.p.m. Measured
frequency of Dyna- jet = 250 cps.

START OF BOOK #2 JEROME LEMElSON (conTinued from book 1) OCTOBER #11, 1950
RECORD OF Conception of Invention: Title: MAgnetic Toy Derrick: & RELEASE
MECHANISM: Description: This toy relates to a derrick which utilizes a magnet
(permanent) to pick up toys or objects of a magnetically susceptible material
and means for releasing said objects without demagnetization. a temporary magnet
has been utilized before & in the art to accomplish this end but this requires a
source of electrical energy, usually a battery which may be worn out rapidly due
to the large current drain by the coil of the magnet. and the constant switching
on and off. Sketch:

In the drawing, a permanent magnet 1 is

### Page 12
placed in a housing 2 (of non-magnetically susceptible material) which is
secured to or part of a toy derrick arm 10. A panel 5 acts as a cover to this
housing and is spring loaded in an open position (as shown) to expose the magnet
1. The panel 5 is connected to a flexible cord ~~8 ~~ 7 at 6 and may be
triggered or released by the operator of the toy to slide over the surface of
the magnet therebye forcing (3) the object which has been picked up off the
magnet and effecting a release. J H L. Oct. 11, 1950 Conception of Invention:
Title: Bubble Blowing Pull Toy: While the following mechansim for this toy are
not worked out in exact detail below they serve to give a description- of the
general principles involved. The idea is to design a pull type toy which has the
proper mechanism for creating & blowing bubbles as the wheels of the toy turn
when the toy is rolled along the ground or pulled. In the sketch on the
following page (over).

October 11, 1950

A wire ring 1 is dipped into bubble liquid reservoir 2 by action of crank 5
which is connected to bend in axle 3, said bend 3 rotates as wheels 8 rotate.
Crank 6 also operating off axle 3 is connected to split shaft 4 which actuates
bellows 2. blowing stream of air thru ring and forming bubbles from film on ring
1. 9 refers to toy figure, in this case shaped like a face. To be developed J
Lemelson Oct. 11, 1950 Oct. 13, 1950 Expanded Plastic Lifereaft (pp. 99,-100
book 1) was described today to Ira Richlin, 945 W. End Ave.

### Page 13

38 ff.) and a more complete model is being prepared for him. He was also shown
the sipping and (draining toy which closes an electrical contact when child
drinks) which he did not approve of. Also present in his office was an inventor
of inverted drap hanging mechanism which Cantor may manufacture.) The magnetic
toy derrick + release (p. 12) may also be made as  constructed as follows 

A magnet 1 picks up toy b. When it is ready to be released, cable or rod 4 is
pulled in direction of arrow drawing magnet into hole and forcing off toy 6. 2
refers to the walls of the receptacle for mag. 1 and 3 to a spring for return of
1. A model has been constructed. J. H. Lemelson. T Remote Magnetic Control
October 28, 1950 The following device for remote (under the board) magnetic
control (see nov. 27, 1949) has been conceived and recorded prior to this in a
self addressed The system of moving magnets about under a thing board or playing
surface so as to move magnets in their braced about on the playing surface has
been derived. Prior (?conederations)untied a vehicle and track placed under the
board. This system utilized a belt and service of pulleys. To facilitate motion
of the belt with attached magnets, a flat belt is utilized with pulley designed
as follows. First diagram on left; reading left to right: "Playing surface,
Belt, Bearing, Pulley, Belt, Magnet. Underneath both diagrams(diagram label):
"Crossectional Views of Pulley, Belt + Magnet Second diagram on the right;
reading left to right: "Surface, Magnet, Belt, Pulley" By mounting a series of
pulleys on a frame or brace and placing below playing surface, and powering,
objects such as toy autos, etc. May be moved around on surface as belt moves. It
may be positive to use a round belt (though not as convenient as flat belt) with
magnets mounted and

### Page 14
(drawings of pulley, belt, magnet components, labeled designed as follows:)
Labels include: Belt Pulley Surface Magnet Belt Groove Pulley in cross section
Groove for magnet Oct. 28, 1950 Conception Idea: Whistling Light-up Toy 
Utilizes a switch which closes when operator blows into whistle and activates or
throws on a light in toy. (See self-addressed letter) Nov. 1, 1950 Magnetic
Switch Toy: See notebook #1 (Feb. 26, 1950) for first conception date. A
completed switch which works was completed in July and it is now being applied
to various toys and games, some of which are recorded in a mailed letter and
witnessed description (i.e. toy mine detector; toy Geiger Counter (simulated);
toy simulated electric eye; etc.).Drawings (patent drawings) have been made and
a pat. application is in process. The author conceives that this switch may be
operated not only by magnetic attraction or repulsion from or towards the
working surface of the toy by an approaching magnet but also by motion of the
moving contact swinging (in direction lateral to the surface of the toy) or in a
direction which is radial or an axis perpendicular to the playing surface, viz:
(drawing labeled with parts 17) (1) Lateral to Surface: Lead in (1) connects to
stationary contact (2). Moving contact (3) has a magnet secured to it and is
caused to swing towards stationary contact (2) when magnet (7) is moved in
direction of arrow (5). (5) is lead in wire to moving contact and (6) designates
a pivot or anchor

### Page 15
for swinging arm (4). (over) Witnessed by: N. Lemelson, Nov. 1, 1950.

### Page 16
(2) Motion radically to surface: Lead in (1) connected to bracket (2) which
holds swinging spring loaded arm (3); mag. Contact point (4) is caused to
contact stationary point (5) by swinging action of magnet (1). Note that (5) may
consist of an annular ring so that (7) may merely approach (4) from any
direction for contact to be made. Above and that on page (17) have disadvantage
of not allowing a prolonged circuit closure as is that shown on page 95 of book
I. By: James H. Hamlin Note: Model of (?) p.88 book 1: Jan. 16, 1950 was

Record of Conception of Invention: Imitation Toy Radar Set + game A toy scope I
set in a cabinet (2) has images flass across it either from a projection of a
shadow from film in optical system of (?) bulb 6 or motion of a motor driven
screen across scope (3). If the screen is utilized, scoring may be accomplished
by pointer 3' which is adjustable by knob (3) and which makes contact with
figures (5) which are painted with conductive paint and have stripes of paint
leading to a band on the side which makes contact with another slider completing
the circuit. (over)

### Page 17
(real radar) (similar real radar) To give a ~~moving effect~~ to the screen, the
scanner may have a varying degree of opaqueness with periphery by:  scanning
green (rotates) when motor is running) clear varying degree of opaqueness around

To give a moving effect to the objects, a period of bright and dark lines placed
on the scanning screen or on the scope face intermeshes with the objects on the
moving screen which are so as to give a dynamic effect (partially old art). When
light is flashed thru the transparent lines the effect is similar to real radar.
To be developed. J Lemelson Nov. 1, 1950 Nov. 2, 1950 The latest model of the
suspended magnetic target game (See book 1, p91 - Feb. 3, 1950) has completed
for Mr.Comtor of Automate Toy company. A search has been made from the Patents
gone three on target games the author believes this game is definitely
patentable. The game consists of a series of magnetic targets anchored to a base
by a flexible cord and suspended in place below other magnets. Means are
supplied for automatically suspending the targes below the magnet once they have
been knocked out of the field. Said means consist of a bar or strip with holes
in it thru which the magnet cord extends riding on dowels or rods in a verticle
plane with means of or raising the bar (with a lever or by merely packing it up
by hand) said action positioning each magnet directly below its suspending
magnet which is mounted on a cross bar. The first model was completed in July
but not recorded JHLemelson Nov,3,1950 Witnessed by H.Lemelson Nov. 10, 1950
Worked today on above mentioned target for a model for Ideal Toy and Novelty Co.

the egg (p.37 book 1) which springs apart when a toy chicken is placed on it, of

Feb .5, 1950 book 1) completing 3 switches; one for a toy geiger counter and one
for a mine detector game. Conception of Formations (1.) Printed circuits  for
Toy Traction. The following method of making toy roadhills, tracks, traction
surfaces etc. Is conceived as a cheap, simple appraoch to the problem of toy
vehicle control and traction. The technique would consist of printing ~~ spp ~~
sputtering, impressing a string or other method of applying a thin metallic

sheet, film or strip to a non metallic surface such as a plastic sheet, wood,
etc which ~~ to ~~ may be shaped so that a toy vehicle ~~ will ~~ (powered by an
electric motor) will seem in a desired direction ~~ down an in ~~. Said
construction would involved the use of two such strips in paralell so that
contact with these strips by the wheels of the vehicle or by other rolling or
sliding contacts will be made to supply current to the motor in the vehicle. The
vehicle would be kept on its course by meditations in the surface or by a
protruding section which would guide the vehicle along a predetermined course.
The circuits could be applied to a large flat surface in one operation to
provide the child with a traffic board or could be applied to sections of
roadbed which could be fastened together by clips or other fasteners To be
developed Nov. 4,50 Nov. 4, 50 Witnessed by: H. Lemelin Nov. 10,1980 Magnetic

Nov. 4, 50 Witnessed by. H. Lemelson 11/10/50 Nov. 6, 1950 re: pp,22,23 A search
of the available literature on printed electrical circuits and the like has
revealed the following information: 1.There are numerous techniques when may be
utilized to apply a metallic coating or strip to a non- conducting surface. 26
such individual methods are tested in National Bureau of Standard Miscellaneous
Publication #192. which includes such techniques as painting,  and spraying
conductive paints and plastics bonded powders, sputtering,

spraying molten metal & , die- cutting foil or sheet metal and attaching with
rivets staples, cement or impressing into molten or soft plastic sheet, etc. It
is conceived that would a number of these techniques would well su be suited to
the devices described on pp. 22 and 23 and to be described, the author having
conceived of a number of other applications. A statement in Nat. Bur. of Stds.
Circular 468 claims that the printed circuit techniques simplify, mechanize &
reduce the cost of sub assembly and assembly and the author conceives where mass
production techniques developed for the toy applications mentioned & to be
mentioned would greatly reduce cost of mfgr, simplify and mechanize the toy
assembly. The conceived to date utilizing printed circuits are: 1) Toy track
sections with means for assembly as described on p p.22, 23 and in self
addressed description (2)Toy Roadbed sections with means for assembly (3) Toy
traffic playing board with people indentations or protruding

### Page 21

painted, printed, sprayed, etc a series of conductive electrical circuits so
arranged that a puck landing on parts of the board (puck made of a ~~ magn ~~
conductive material) will complete a circuit and score with a bell, light, etc
The puck or dart may be a magnet so that the game may be played on the verticle
(with the board on verticle) Other games to be recorded when time permits. J H
Lemelson Nov 6, 1950 Witnessed by: H.Lemelson 11/10/50 Nov. 9, 1950 The rubber
stamp rack coceived and recorded about a month ago consisting of a series of of
lateral flanges or (means for laterally positioning a series of objects to a
rack said objects hanging by magnetic attraction to said racks) was shown in
completed patent drawing form and engineering product sketches to the following
members of Roovers Brothers, Inc, 3611 - 14th Ave Brooklyn, N.Y.

1 Mr. Payne, production manager. 2 Miss Mack, secretery to manager of company. A
call today to Mr. Payne, who was quite interested in the device will verify if
the manager or owner of the company will desire to manufacture the item. A
search of my records has revealed that I possibly may have failed by error to
record this invention in detail prior to this date. the device was conceived
about the end of September 1950, a model was completed week later and a patent
drawing was completed about a week ago and copies were made by photostating. One
copy is missing from my files and I may have mailed this to my self though
misplaced it. I recall making a sketch & description which I will search for. I
am preparing a patent application on the device, at present working on the
claims. My brother Hoard ~~ was ~~ has witnessed work on this and he visited
Roovers brothers today with the drawings & description. Essentially, the
broadest claim I can conceive of today (based on the results of a search of
stamp racks, holding devices particularly magnetics holders in Witnessed by: H.
Lemelson 11/10/50

### Page 22

the search room of the US Patent about a week ago. Pertinent Patents are 2158221
1809195 1562369 Essentially the invention consists of providing means for
~~prepositioning~~ attracting a series of oblong objects such as rubber stamps
(hand operated) to a rack~~s~~ and holding in place by the use of magnets, said
objects extending in a generally downward direction (hanging down), with means
provided for prepositioning each oblong object and preventing lateral
displacement. The combination of this means holding said object from swinging
sidewards or positioning in racks plus the magnetic attraction makes a simple
easy to use holding device. Said means for prepositioning and preventing lateral
displacement or swing may consist of a strip of metal at right angles to the
contact surface and circumventing the object near its upper end or
semicircumventing it if it is desired to position the object from the side, A
sketch of a typical stamp rack would be

as follows: (Similar to one of pat. drawings)

In the above drawings: a rubber stamp 1 contains a magnet 4 attached to its
handle (in the ~~ t ~~ upper end) so as to permit the stamp to hang from a
magnetically susceptible material or surface. The rack shelf 3 is of this
magnetically susceptible material or may be

### Page 23
be made of plastic or non mag susceptible material with a magnet embedded or
attached in it around the perimeter where objects are to hang. Semi-circular
strip 2 is used as a prepositioner, and it may extend beyond the edge of 3 so
that the user turning top may has his positioning of 1 simplified. The above
rack may also be applicable to tools and the like, or any oblong objects that
can be hung by magnets. Jerome Lemelson Nov. 10, 1950 Witnessed by: H Lemelson

1951 March 18, 1951 Record of Invention: Spray Nozzle (Utilizing porous material
such as porous metal, ceramic, etc). This invention was conceived at least four
months ago and disclosed shortly thereafter to H. Lemelson & R. Kraashaur ~~ er
~~ of N.Y.U. It consists essentially of directing a stream(s) of high velocity
air on a porous surface which has a non clogging liquid continually ~~ poring ~~
feeding thru the pores of the solid, preferably under pressure. The advantages
of this technique over conventional nozzles are (1) economy of manufacture (2)
larger area of liquid dispersion (3) flexibility of design permitting an area
source of a fine mist. A design for a typical nozzle follows on the next page:
The principle involved is:

stream of air from nozzle (1) porous sheet fluid (under pressure) duct for fluid

A Typical design (one of many possible variaTions)

Side View (1)

Air Holes (4) (1) Bottom View

Note: This device was described to R. Krashaar in Feb. 1951. JHL. J. in may 1951

A series of holes (4) direct air under pressure so as to impinge obliquely

### Page 29
on the tapered conical nozzle section (1) which is made of a porous material.
Liquid under pressure (3) is constantly forced thru the pores of the nozzle
section and blown off the outer surface in a fine mist by the jets of air. By

May 6,1951 The following application of a free piston engine device has been
conceived. It is conceived that the free piston engine may be utilized to do
work of an oscillating nature - i.e - apply an intermittent force such as in (1)
a rivet gun (2) "compressed air" type hammer (Joels hammer), etc. The
arrangement in its simplest form would be something like the following

In the above figure, A+B refers to pistons connected by rod (1), Fuel and air
are injected into cylinder head areas (J) + (K) and ignited by spark plugs (S).
F+E refer to ~~ slide ~~ exhaust ports which are uncovered by pistons as they
advance away from head. (I) refers to ~~ spaces ~~ volumes between baffle (L)
which separates the two chambers from each other. The compression in these
volumes due to each piston advancing against plate (L) may be utilized to pum a
fluid to do work, to pump air or gases to cool the engine, to compress a fuel
for May 6-1951 fuel injection into each cylinder head, to compress an ignitable
fuel air mixture which will do work in compressing the pa gases for the next
stroke, etc Rod H extends thru a hole(well sealed) in (M) cylinder head and is
utilized to due work as the pistons oscillate back & forth. A single piston
arrangement is Spring In the drawing, Piston (P) is rigidly connected to shaft
(H) and loaded against spring (K) to maintain top dead center position
(compression) fuel is injected thru fuel injection system together with air (air
may come in thru a subpiston (not shown) in (P). which opens on the upstrobe
when ignition plug (S) explodes piston compress spring (K) when it reaches its
botton dead position it has already

### Page 31
slid past exhaust port (E) exhausting gases. The spring then returns the piston
to its top position, compressing incoming gases. Shaft H provides the oscilating
jabbing motion for work during operation. Note: Diaphram type metallic spring
may be  in place of coil spring shown. Volume V may be  for pumping. By Jerome
Lemelson May 6- 1951 Witnessed by: Howard Lemelson May 6, 1951 May 23- 1951 Free
Piston Engine Electric Generator It is conceived that the free-piston type
internal combustion engine may be utilized ~~ to ~~ in combination with the
necessary current producing components to produce an alternating or direct
current. Since this involves considerable development & design work ~~ in volume
~~ to arrive at an optimum operating current generating unit, only the basic
ideas for the designs will be presented at this time in this notebook pending
further ~~ full se ~~ design consideration by the inventor.

May 23-1951 The inventor is aware of prior free piston engine development by the
French Inventor Pescara whose firm has manufactured over 1000 hot air compressor
units. The free piston-type i.e. engine has numerous advantages over the
conventional piston - crank shaft engine. Simplicity of design, and fabrication,
and the possibility of ataining greater efficiencies due to less frictional
losses (no bearings, etc) and possibility of ataining higher compressibility of
fuel-air mixtures prior to ignition lable the engine type as outstanding. The
present known free piston engine designs are: A Use of two (short) free floating
pistons with combustion in three regions viz. (Pescara, German, U.S.
experimental types)

Fig. 1 In the above very simplified sketch, ~~ for ~~ a combustable mixture is
injected into zones 1, 2, & 3. This pistons oscillate back & forth as an
explosion occurs in zone 2 forcing pistons to

### Page 32
compress mixtures

### Page 33
in zones 1 & 2. At the proper instant, these mixtures are ignited forcing the
two pistons towards each other compressing a ~~ n ~~ combustible mixture forced
into that zone thru injector I2. This mixture is then ignited. forcing the
pistons away from each other again. E1, E2, E3, E4 refer to exhaust ports where
the gases are expelled or exhausted hot & at a pressure considerably greater
than atmospheric to do work. This is essentially the present day free piston
engine without the showing the more complex intake and exhaust slide valve
arragement ~~ uit ~~ utilized. If pistons 1 & 2 are designed as follows;

This whole assembly Formerly piston 1 Zone A 1a Shaft A 1b Fig. 2 it is seen
that there is a zone (Zone A) between the pistons 1a & 1b which is not in the
hot burning gas zone. If an interface or plate is places in this zone, and the
proper valving for intake and exhaust are installed, work may be done on a cold
fluid such as air, oil, etc. In addition, ~~ with ~~ Shaft A may be utilized to
do mechanical work if the interface is May 23-1951 removed. By linking or
recharge a shaft at an angle to said shaft A and extending it beyond the walls
of the engine eyelander Basic Design of Tree Piston Engine as a ColdPenny. Fig.3
shows this arrangement designed to pump cold air or fluids. The intake and
exhaust ducting are shown in very basic form. *Diagram reading left to right*
V1, V(1A) , I IB, V (1B) (1B), V2, Notevaluing is not shown from region other
than (1B) (L), E(1B) Operation may be explained as fall by looking at region 1B
between piston (1B) and separating plate (L). Combustion takes place in V2. The
assembly including piston 1B moves to the left. One way value I(1B) which is a
fluid intake value closes and exhaust value E(1B) opens permitting the fluid (as
for example) in the chambers to flow out due to the compression by piston (1B).
The combination change in region

### Page 34
V1 is then ignited forcing the assembly to the right, intake valve 1B opens
permitting fluid to be drawn in by the over expansion; at the the same time, one
way exhaust valve is forced closed. The cycle then repeats, also in the other 3
regions between the pistons and plate L. If a liquid is utilzed it may be ducted
to turn a turbine, into a fluid drive unit, do  do work as in ~~f ~~ lifting,
etc. Other components of a system utilizing a fluid would be; a hydraulic
accumulator to permit steady flow (acclimate the pulsating flour), a fluid drive
unit, etc. The designing would also include proper ducting of the unit so that
flow from each volume would follow the next for smoother flow. Use of the
freepiston engine as an impact tool has been described on pp. 40 & 41. Other
proposed uses are: a. in sawing - there is ample reciprocating oscillatory
motion to do sawing work. b. as a drill - this would require conversion of the
reciprocating motor to rotary. c. For Generating Electrical Energy: Several of
the basic design are as follows - See next page.

May 23-1951 I Placing the armature magnet (magnetic field) directly on the
piston or piston connecting shaft. Field windings would then either surround the
cylinder of the free piston engine or positioned near said cylinder or possibly
be placed inside cylinder in the zone between the pistons in such a manner that
the pistons may travel without interference One arrangement is as follows:

Since the frequency of the AC. pulses are dependent on the frequency of
oscillations of the free piston arrangements, a speed regulator device may be
necessary for constant AC. pulses, or use of a rectifier will give a direct
current. The use of sliding type brushes may enable permit use of an electro
magnet (Armature winding) to replace the permanent magnet.

### Page 35
An May 23-1951 Another arrangement is as follows. In which an extension of the
piston or (interconnecting piston rods) extends beyond the cylinder wall thru a
slot in said wall and said armature winding or permanent magnet is connected to
said extension as follows:

Motion of the permanent magnet back & forth with respect to the field windings
(which may surround the permanent magnet (slotted also) creates an alternating
current in the field circuit. Note that when compared to the conventional rotary
motor generator (combination, we see that all frictional losses in bearings,
brushes etc are not present in this arrangement More electrical energy per lb.
of fuel is derived for use. Future designs will consider complex arrangements of
the above. By Jerome Lemelson May 23, 1951 Witnessed by: Howard Lemelson May 24,

June 20-1951 The following idea was conceived today and revealed to James
Jeffress as a possible method of reducing the pressure near the exhaust of an
internal combustion engine for better scavenging. Design of the exhaust port so
that compressed gases either from the combustion chamber or from a section of
the engine in which there is a certain degree of compression pass out in the
exhaust area a high speeds therebye utilizing the principles of jet ejection to
help scavenge by reduction of pressure & carrying along exhaust gases. The

August 5-1951 (1.) Regarding a magnetic holder which was conceived last Febuary

~~m~~ by mail or in this book. I intend to utilize a permanent magnet in
combination with a correct device to secure optical instruments to a ~~cast~~
magnetically attractive base such as the flat surface of an optical bed, or an
interferometer base. This would require ~~some~~mechanism for reducing the force
of attraction between the magnet in the device and the bed ~~and~~ or for
removing the former from the bed without scratching the surface or having to
exert too much direct force. I intend to do this by either using a screw or
lever arrangement to pry the magnet off the surface or by correctly engaging and
disengaging a magnet or magnetically susceptible material to reduce the power of
the holding magnet. (2.) Regarding my ~~automa~~ remote controlled doll

Oct. 18-1951 #1 The following ideas in toy blocks have been conceived and will
be shown to Milton Schataf who is production supervisor for Greyshaw, Inc. a
manufacturer of plastic toys and blocks. Drawings and photostats will be made:

Clear Block Wall Toy Block balls collect at bottom Plastic insert giving a path
down the wall of the block along which small balls or particles may travel when
the plo block is properly fitted A drawing is being made of this which will be
recorded witnessed and recorded by mail. Idea #2. Musical Blocks. It is proposed
to create musical notes in blocks or toys by having small pellets or balls,
falling from a storage space, empinge on a sounding board or bell. viz: See
diagram on next page.

### Page 45

Description: October 19th (continued) The small particles or balls A collect in
chamber C thru holes H in partition P which separates C from the main region R
of the clock and which forms a downwardly slanting chute with hold D, just large
enough to permit one ball to drop thru at a time. The balls A flow thru hole D
and strike bell or sounder B, thus causing a continuous series of sounds. To
return the balls to the chamber, the block is tilted on its head, balls A roll
thru hole A into C and the cycle is repeated. As a toy a ~~ multitude ~~ several
holes may be used with the balls of various sizes fallen thru respective holes
and impinging on different bells or sounders to give different notes. Jerome H.
Lemelson Oct 19- 1951 Oct 20-1951 witnessed by H. Lemelson Oct. 20, 1951 I saw
Ed Baggott of Ideal Toy Co. this morning and discussed and showed him drawings
of my patent on Toy . One of the things we discussed makes

Doll & Moving Mouth: About three months ago I conceived of a doll with a mouth
that moves as it utters a sound and recorded on a sheet which was mailed to
myself. As I showed this to Mr. Bagott Chief Engineer of Ideal Toy Company about
two months ago (Re: p. 56, Aug 51) and, he has not acted in good faith recently
regarding a mechanism which I suggested, I am recording variations on this as
follows: Baggott avoided the topic when I saw him on October 20th and I am
hereby recording these variations for my protection in the future. (1 Doll with
moving mouth and sounding mechanism. According to my original conception this
was to be accomplished by using a shaped or perforated tape on which an arm was
to ride, said arm the movement of the jaw when the doll talked. A simpler
arrangement would be to utilize a gravity operated sounder such as those used to
make a crying noise, which would operate the mouth moving mechanism. viz.

(Over)

### Page 46
Operation: When the doll is tilted, the bellows tends to return to its normal
position, Its weight is also connected to an arm which is connected by a bubage
arrangement to move the jaw when the weight drops. The anbage may cause one
movement or a more complex opening and closing of the lips synchronized with the
sound. (To be developed very shortly) Laughing Doll: A simple arrangement
whereby a doll could be made to laugh when shaken involves the use of a doll
cryer with preferably a base tone and a stroke so limited that a brief noise
will be emitted when the mechanism is tilted with the doll or when the doll is
shaken. The stroke of the bellows must me short so that the doll will not cry
when shaken or tilted but will give off a series of chuckle like noises when
shaken rapidly Another variation on this would be to drive said bellows with a
motor or by a mechanism activated by the childs winding or pulling a toy. By
Jerome Lemelson Oct 23-51 Witnessed by: H Lemelson Nov. 22, 1957 Note: the doll

1952 Witnessed by: H. Lemelson 2/29/52 Feb. 13, 1952 The following items were
recently conceived. Rubber or Plastisol (polyvenyl-chloride) covered materials.
A number of items have been conceived which utilize a base item covered by a
layer of plastic material such as a plastisol (polyvenyl chloride) or rubber.
Covering the item with the rubber or rubber like layer which is actually bonded
to the surface gives it unique new qualities on permits the performing of a past
function in a cheaper and more efficient manner. and perhaps permits the item to
be fabricated more cheaply. Item (1)- ~~Plo~~Polishing or Cleaning Granule A
ball granule made either of a solid lump of a rubber or rubber like material
such as a plasticol (polyvenylchlor) (over)

### Page 59

layer of the plastisol conceivably may be ableyed  as a cleaning or polishing
aid ~~agent~~ when used ~~welt~~as a shot which is blasted or otherwise forced
against the surface to be cleaned or polished and preferably in combination with
a polishing or cleaning agent or abrasive. Diagram of rubber like shot or
tumbling agent.

Item: #2: Seal for solid containers (such as glass, etc) It is conceived that a
container and its cover which are made, for example of ~~faile~~fairly rigid
material, may be effectively sealed by coating the contacting surfaces with a
rubber or rubber like material such as a plastisol and possibly shaping the

and other formable materials has been conceived utilizing magnetic fluids or
fine particles which are frozen in shape by magnetic forces and then ~~ as ~~
utilized as male and (or) female dies to form the material. The procedure for
their fabrication would be as follows.

(A)~~form to be stamped~~shape to be formed C partition (A) partition (B)
magnetic fluid (particles) (fluid to be heated for thermo forming of plastics,
etc.) Housing ~~ The housing is placed in a magnetic field A magnetic field is
produced around the housing after the form (A) is inserted as shown with a
partition (B) surrounding the form so that the two halves of the die may be
separated when frozen by the magnetic ~~ field ~~ forces. The die halves are
then separated, a sheet of material to be formed is placed between them and they
are brought together in a press to make the resulting form. Coils of magnetic
field producing may actually run thru magnetic fluid: c for added field strength
Impact Forming: It is conceived that thin sheets may be bent or formed about a
die by causing a fluid to impinge at great dynamic pressure (as in impact)
against the sheet which is placed over a male or female form. The whole
operation would preferably ~~viz.~~ take place in a closed vessle. Witnessed by:

February 29, 1952 Rivets: The following ideas in rivets were conceived several
weeks ago and are now being recorded: Pressure Sealing Rivets: The following
rivet designs were conceived for application where there is pressurization and
breakage is not desirable. ~~ at ~~ In other words they are designed to seal the
riveted section in the area of the rivet hole. Several types of sealing rivets
are conceived

Type I Type 1 Type 1 ~~ set Fig. 1 (IN PLACE & sealing) (1) In the figure 1
above, the rivet has a conventional shank 1 & head 2 which is stepped from
section 4 to 5. The step (4-5) is cut circumferentially around the outer
perimeter of the head; section 4 remaining to bear against the face of the work
while the rivet is set. The normal ~~ A compressible ring or washer 3

having a thickness or width normally greater than the axial width of the step is
provided and preferably secured to the head so that the riveter merely has to
press the a rivet into the hole in the work and upset the shank, compressing the
washer as the rivet is set therebye sealing off the hole into which the rivet
fits. From fig. 2 it can be seen that the compressed washer ~~ woul ~~ seals off
the space under the head after the rivet is set. Variations: The following
variations of this principle have been conceived: (2) washer close to shanks:

washer should be slightly smaller than the groove in which it seats to

### Page 65
allow it to expand outward when compressed By Jerome H Lemelson 2/29/52
witnessed & understoodly by: Helen Kahry 2/29/52 Howard Lemelson 2/29/52 (over)

end of shank (for blind type rivets) VIZ:

sleeve protects inside end. After upsetting rivets EXPLOSIVE TYPE RIVET UPSET

Conception of Invention: The following ideas regarding plastics, there
processing and treatment have been conceived. In general the ideas have been
conceived as a result of the recent announcement about the "plastigels" (re:
Modern Plastics Magazine" Jan 1952, putty-like' plastic substances which may be
formed at room temperature under low pressure and hardened at temperatures of
300 to 400F. It is conceived by the author that a variety of new products and
applications June 4-1952 of these plastigels may be made. In particular, the use
of "electronic" heat may be utilized to fabricate these new products ~~and p~~
and a variety of new processes. At this writing , the ideas may be broken down
into the following categories. I. Plastigels ( or other plastics) combined
mechanically with other compounds for (a) new uses and effects and (b) color
combinations of plastigels to create new effects and products II. New ~~teh~~
techniques for fabricating plastics such as plastigels by radio or electronic
heat III. Fusing plastigels with ultrasonic waves. Describing in more detail: I.
Plastigels combined and processed with soft vinyl (poly vinyl chloride. A number
of new products are conceived at present from time to time I expect to add
others to the following list: (a) As a ridgitizing or reenforcing agent. (1)
Button hole reenforcement: It is conceived that a J Lemelson June 4-52 Julius
Lemelson June 4-52

reenforce the butt hole and protect it against easy tearing of the thin vinyl
sheet. vz.

4-52 Cheap Mold Making Technique Reference Figure:

A B C D Figure I The technique involves (Fig. I) taking a base form (A) which is
a pattern a little smaller than the pattern desired to be molded-, applying a
layer (B) which may be, for example, a metal shell which is sprayed, or plated
on (A); adding (coating) another layer of a material (C) over the form (B)
~~which then~~ the outer surface of which then become the base of another shell
(D) which may be another metallic layer which is sprayed or electrolytically
plated on. Sheels (B) and (D) thus become the male and female part of the mold
after layers (C) and base (A) are removed. Julius Lemelson June 4 1952 mor
(over) J. Lemelson June 4-52

### Page 84
a technique may be necessary to reenforce both (B) & (D). (A) may be left in (B)
or another material poured in when (A) is removed. To reenforce (D) (Fig. II

(E) (D) (F) Fig. II place it in a frame and pour or add reenforcing substance
    (F) about (D) which solidifies making a strong female mold section. The male
    section is now aligned with the structure and aligning pins or other means
    are added completing the mold. This would be a substitute for slush molding

conceived prior to and recorded by witnessed, self addressed papers on June
28-1951 has been built and works fine. It will be shown in one witnessed by
Howard Lemelson Dec. 16,1952

or more of its intended play arrangements to Mr. B.F. Michtom of Ideal Toy Corp.
Description of Device:

This was shown to and discussed with Mark Michtom of Ideal Toy Corporation on
Jan 26, 53 JHL. Feb. 1, 1953 Also Ben Weildstem of Palmer Plastics Fig. 1 shows
the mechanism which is classified as a "delay release catapult mechanism". It
comprises essentially a spring loaded arm 1 pivotably mounted on a base 7 having
a suction cup 4 secured to one end thereof and a holding means 5 for the object
6 to be catapulted. A suction cup 4 secured to the end of 1 is pressed against
the surface of 7 against the tension of spring 3. After a brief delay, the
spring 3 tension overcomes the suction cup holding force and the arm swings up
in the direction of the arrow A causing the ball 6 to be catapulted. Note: the
suction cup 4 may be replaced by a ~~ pie ~~ lump of tacky substance such as tar
or gum which holds down arm 1 until the tension of the spring over comes it. The
spring 2 and pivot

Oct. 30-1948 have been conceived by the author in connection with his work in
jet propulsion for Project Squid at New York University. These records are being
kept by the author for the following purposes. 1. As a reference aid to the
author in his future work. 2. To establish a date of conception for possible
patent application in the future in devices relating to jet engine designs. 3.
To establish proof that the author has conceived of, and, is the inventor of
these various devices. In such cases where the author has collaborated with
others on the project with such designs, or where other persons are solely
responsible for the design, the author will make mention of such in writing.
This notebook is not intended by the author to be used in recording test run
measurements and experimental results which will only by of interest to the
project director for administration purposes. Another notebook (#2) will be used
for administrative purposes. This book is a personal record of the author
designed to serve the above 3 purposes and in which the author may enter any

inventions as applied to the field of jet propulsion. Entries will be made by

under his present work schedule. Experimental results will be entered in this
book when necessary to show that a design has been reduced to practice or is in

Nov. 1, 1948 A. Elimination of Part F. It is conceived that part F, the rotary
disc valve behind the grid, might be eliminated completely from the setup and
still maintain engine operation. The author plans to experiment with this idea
in the Dyna-Jet and in the experimental grid type jet engine to be built. B.
Fuel Injection at E: It is conceived that it may

be necessary to inject fuel at E (in the secondary combustion region) to sustain
operation of this engine. Possible Applications of the Grid to Other Jet

JAN. 31-1949 On this date the author conceived of a method of cooling and
preserving the grid structure. One of the experimental grids (made of 3/8" sheet
brass) melted during operation of the engine. To protect the grid, the author
suggests that fuel to be introduced in the primary and secondary region thru
this grid. This might be the point which will make the grid workable in the
combustion chamber. DIAgram:

Dec. 1049 NACA TN 1969  Comparative Drag Tests. NACA technicians dropping
bomb-like missile with wings to measure drag  (sectioned) of various shapes &
contours. TN-273  Newton & D'essergulliers dropped glass spheres in free fall
in water. TN-810 Advancement of art of designing airplanes particularly new
types that will have desired flying characteristics has long been handicapped by
the complexity of stability and control theory & by general unpredictable nature
of some of fundamental derivatives involved  Realizing the advantages of being
able to study stability and control problems with a free-flying model in the
controlled conditions of a wind tunnel, the NACA in 1937 completed the
development of a 5-foot free flight wind tunnel. Variation of any dimension of
the model can readily be accomplished and the effects on flying qualities
determined. 12-foot free flight tunnel 1/2 scale P-36.

### Page 15
April 14  1950 Process For Finishing Aluminum with a Lustrous or Polished
Surface: The author proposes the following process for putting a highly
reflective and polished surface on aluminum and aluminum objects. It is the
desire to such a process where aluminum is to be used as a structure and as an
ornamental surface. At the time of this writing, no method has been developed
whereby aluminum may be chrome plated. The following technique may serve the
purpose and experiments will be conducted to ascertain if it may be successfully
and satisfactorily accomplished. ~~ Ch ~~ Step I  Chroming the aluminum surface
either by the present techniques or by the development of a technique whereby
the process may be accomplished at a lower temperature (solution temperature).
Step II  Polishing the chromised surface by: (a) Mechanical buffing (b) Acid
cleaning and polishing (c) Buffing or polishing the surface by using a fine
grained polishing or buffing compound suspended in a jet of high velocity steam
or air. This

would differ from sand blasting in that the working particles would be much
finer, they would be suspended in a liquid, fluid such as steam or other gas
which would be ejected through small nozzles at a very high velocity, impinging
on the surface and polishing it. Jerome Lemelson Apr. 14, 1950

July 18, 1956 Starting a brief recording of the patents and inventions I am
working on at this time. Classified as follows Classification Number J.56-1 This
refers to my ~~ to ~~ patent application to be entitled Video Magnetic Recording
which is about two thirds completed at the this writing The invention pertains
to video picture and tracking signals recorded on magnetic tape and means for
manipulating thereof and performing inspection and computational operations
thereof J56-2 This refers to an invention conceived over a week ago ~~ with a sm
~~ and modifications conceived today for irradiating methods for the plastics
and other materials which change their chemical and physical characteristics ~~
upon ~~ It is known to irradiate various polymers, silicone rubber, and other
Jerome Lemelson July 18 - 1956

### Page 20
materials with x-rays, or high energy electrons to change their physical
characteristics. Ordinary polyethylene for example when irradiated changes to a
more durable plastic when irradiated with electrons in the range of several
million electron will be increased in its ability to withstand heat, improved in
durability, hardness, etc. An article (page 1, column 8 of July 18th 1956 issue
of the Wall Street Journal) mentions that Ford Motor Company can concentrate
dye~~ s ~~ change ~~ to ~~ neutral white paint, etc to colored paint by playing
a controlled radiation (electron) gun over the paint. The following are methods
of are~~ a ~~ radiating a specific part of an article, leaving the rest of the
article or the area thereof untouched by radiation or irradiated to a lesser
degree for the purposes of (a) changing the physical and chemical
characteristics of certain areas or parts of said article or (h) providing
different colors on said article by radiation.

Fig. 1

Fig. 2 Witnessed N.J. 7/18/56

Fig. 1 shows an article of manufacture (A) which is made of a plastic or other
material, or coated with a ~~ m ~~ paint whereby said material or coating
exhibits improved physical characteristics and (or) change of color or shade
after irradiation by high energy electrons or other atomic particles such as
those produced b a Van der Gaff generator A mask (M) is positioned between said
article (A) and a source (SR) of said radiation, said mask acting to absorb all
or part of the energy fro SR except at an opening(s) H in said Mask. The surface
of (A) opposite the opening H thus receives a greater degree of radiation than
the rest of (A.) The mask may be made of any material which will absorb the
desired degree of said radiation for a given thickness. It may be made of lead,
or any suitable metal. It may also comprise photsenstive glass or plastic having
one or more developed or etched areas thereof ~~ thru ~~ capable of absorbing
more of the radiant energy from the source SR than the other areas thereof.
Another conceived use of such a mask and process of radiation is in the
manufacture of articles of plastic having different areas of a single shape with
different physical characteristics. Jerome Lemelson 3/15/56 Witnessed NJ 7/18/56

### Page 21
As stated, ordinary polyethylene when irradiated with high energy atomic
radiation, x-rays, etc. becomes more rigid and exhibits improved physical and
chemical characteristics By using a mask of the types illustrated on p.30, a
sheet of polyethylene plastic may be produced by radiation which has an area of
thereof which is rigid and an area or areas which are flexible (not irradiation
or not as much irradiated as the other). A multitude of new products are
conceived with such a construction such as (a) plastic clothing, containers,
covers, closures, etc. Which ~~ are ~~ have a flexible area or areas supported
by integrally formed area or areas thereof which are rigid (by irradiation).
Typical area. (1) ~~ toothpast ~~ Dispensing tube

(2) Clothing, capes, coves, with rigid (irradiated) ribs (irradiated) for
support Buttonhole areas irradiated for strengthening. Borders, seams, etc.
irradiated for strengthening, etc. Jerome Lemelson July 19-'56

July 24, 1956 ~~ Project (J-56-1) ~~ Display Device The following display device

as in outdoor advertizing.

cantelevered areas ~~ 11 ~~ or flaps 11 form of said flaps 11 are movable by a

velocity as does out-ofdoors ambient air. Explained to me by J.H. Lemelson x

narrow neck 11' and is joined by said neck to the sheet 10. The neck 11 is
preferably of such a dimension that the degree of ambient or surrounding

breeze used to displace the flap 10 will effect its motion without effecting
permanent deformation of said material or tearing it at said neck 11' so that
the ~~ love ~~ lower section 11" of the flap 11 will return to a pre ~~ deformed
~~ displaced position and hang by gravity when no breeze or air is present or
will swing in the other direction relative to the sheet 10 as illustrated in the
edge view Fig 2 when the direction of the ambient breeze shifts. The neck 11'
thus acts as a cantilevered spring which coacts with the weight of the lower
section 11" of the flap 11 to return the flap to its predisplaced position. ~~

Mar 21, 1957 Conception of devices for employing shock waves in process
manufacture, testing and control: The following devices were conceived about 5
months ago in the employment of shock waves to initiate or effect chemical and
physical change on materials or work in process. Definitions of terms SW= A
shock wave created in a fluid by spark discharge, chemical reaction (explosion),
or mechanical compression of the fluid. SWN  Shock wave created in a duct and
adapted to travel essentially normal to the walls of said duct along said duct
unless otherwise specified. DT  Duct in which one or a multiple of shock waves
are created in rapid succession or at any specified frequencies and travel from
one part of said duct to another part or end of said duct. Jerome H Lemelson Mar
21/57 J. M. B. Friediman 3/21/57

DTEW  End wall of a duct in which shock waves are created. VI An inlet valve
for passing a gas, liquid or flowable material into a duct or chamber in which
shock waves are created. Material to be operated on, chemically or physically
changed by said shock wave or waves. VE  An outlet valve from a duct or chamber
in which shock waves may be created or passed by, for the removal of a fluid or
flowable solid material or solid article admitted thereto to contact with or be
operated on by said shock waves. Other terms will be defined in the
descriptions. Device #1: (over)

### Page 27
J. H. L. 3/21/57 M.B. Friedman 3/21/57

### Page 28
Device #1

Fig. 1 In fig. 1, two shock tubes DT-1 and DT2 are placed end to end in endwise
alignment so that the shockwaves SWN-1 and SWN2 created in each will approach
each other. By timing the formation of each shock in the upstream end of its
respective tube they may be made to appear at the working zone ZN (located at
the end of each tube) at essentially the same time. The fluid in zone ZN will
thus be compressed by the action of both waves converging thereon. If the waves
SWN1 and SWN2 are created by resonating effects in each tube (i.e.- if each tube
is the exhaust end of a pulse jet, free piston engine exhaust or any type of
tuned or J.H.L. 3/21/57 M.B. Friedman 3/21/57

resonating travelling wave tube in which shock waves are created and amplified
as a result of said resonation) and if both tubes are operating in
synchronization with each other (i.e.- the intermittent or repetitive shocks ~~
waves arrive ~~ waves arrive at ZN at the same time) then both tubes will act
essentially as closed end or quarter wave tubes as the shocks will reflect off
each other upon impact ~~ and travel ~~ or intersecting and travel back the
tubes. Valves V-1 and VE are secured to the walls of the joined tubes DT-1 and
DT-2 adjacent said working zone ZN and are adapted to respectively admit and
exhaust a fluid to said zone. The notation W-1 refers to a fluid in duct P-1
prior to entry into said zone ZN and W-2 to the fluid exhausted from zone ZN.
This fluid (i.e. the fluid entering thru valve V-1 may be the same as that
already in the shock tubes or it may be a different fluid. The fluid in JHL
3/21/57 M.B. Friedman 3/21/57

### Page 29
each time said wave reaches said wall. The inlet and exhaust valves V-1 and V-E
are provide to inject a fluid or fluids into the working zone and remove the
resulting fluid therefrom both preferably operating to open and close at
predetermined rate or otherwise as described. In Fig. 3, the working zone ZN"
comprises a chamber of greater crossection than the duct DT into which a greater
volume of fluid may be infected at any angle and in which said fluid may collect
(if a liquid or residue) such as in the illustrated sump zone SZ. It is noted
that such a chamber may be provided in the working zone ZN of Fig. 1 between the
two shock tubes DT-1 and DT-2 In Fig. 3, the fluid infector or valve V-1 is
shown mounted so as to inject said fluid at essentially right angles to the
shock waves generated in the duct DT. Said fluid may be injected in this manner
to enhance or augment any resonating effects set up in duct DT which augment or
create MBF 3/21/57

the resulting shock waves.

Fig. 4 I In Fig 4, the working zone is provided as the interior of a spherical
chamber SC preferably made of ~~ met ~~ cast metal and water cooled if necessary
to control the internal temperatures. Shown secured to said sphere and
communicating with its interior are four tubes DT-1 to DT-4 the longitudinal
axis of which converge at the center of the sphere SC of said tubes are mounted
so as to be 120 degrees apart from lack other, and the shock waves created on
each JHL 3/21/57 MBF 3/21/57 MB 9/21 57

### Page 30
are normal to the axes of each tube, and all shockwaves the shockwave in each
tube arrives at the point where the tube joins the sphere simultaneously then
said shock waves will eventually form an equilateral pyramid of decreasing
volume with a center the center of the sphere. By injecting a fluid ot flowable
material thru a fifth duct P-1 towards the center of the sphere said fluid may
be caught between said four shocks and will be greatly compressed by the action
of all four shocks converging on said fluid. Multiple injection ducts or nozzles
similar to P-1 and all aimed towards the center of the sphere may be provided to
improve the efficiency of the device One or more exhaust or take off valves may
be provided at the low point or at any predetermined point on the wall of the
sphere and  opened and closed at predetermined time intervals JHS 3/21/57 MPB
3/21/57

Methods of Extruding Aluminum etc July 8, 1957 The following ideas have been
conceived concerning the extrusion of metals and plastics. A patent application
will be worked on in the near future describing & claiming these ideas. 1 - Stop
Extrusion It is conceived to provide means associated with an extrusion die for
varying the crossectional area of the die hole during extrusion to produce
elongated shapes of varying crossection (which vary with length). Such shapes as

processing or fabrication of said products. (1) Tubes of varying crosssection

is shown, a tube 15 having a seamless wall 40 ~~with~~ of a constant wall

interior of said tube as shown and are an integral formation of the material of
said wall 40. The solid sections 42 are formed by axial manipulation of the
mandrel utilized to extrude said tubing in the extrusion die in the manner to be
described. Said sections 42 may be provided to serve one or more of several
purposes. They may be used to strengthen or stiffen said tubing per se in or in
~~area~~ lengths thereof where greatest loads are to be exerted such as at ~~p~~
sections where other structural members are to be secured thereto and exert a
load thereon. The solid sections 42 may be provided where it is desired to drill
partially or completely thru the walls of said tubing for securing it to other
members with fasteners or the like

or where it is desired to weld, braze or solder said tubing to other members.
The solid section when machined or operated on will provide a structure much
stronger than the thinner and weaker tube wall 40. Since section 42 may be made
solid thru and thru the wall thickness of the rest of the tubing may be less
than conventional tubing used for the same purpose. Sections 42 may be provided
at equal distances along the length of the tube and serve as stiffeners for the
walls thereof or at predetermined points in the length of the tube in accordance
with the later fabrication requirements of said tube. If the tubing 15 is to be
used as a fluid conductor, or storage medium one or more sections 42 may be used
to confine the fluid to a length of the tube and may also be used as a base for

Sept. 1, 1957 Additional Material to Be Added to the specification of the
invention of pp. 1677 p. 71 to end of page add (A) Also shown in Fig. 71 is a
marking device 39 secured to the frame 2 of the press and positioned adjacent
the extruding tube 15 for providing a mark on the exterior of said tube which is
indicative of the variations in internal crossection. For example, if a solid
plug-like member section 42 is formed at a particular length or section of the
extrusion said section may not be easily discernable from the exterior of the
tube by visual means and tube is not made of a translutransparent material. It
may therefore be desirable to mark the section of the tube where the section 42
occurs in the event it is desireed to drill thru or cut into the section 42. The
marker 39 may be any well known marking device which is solonoid operated and
may comprise simply a solonoid stamp for putting an indented mark in the
exterior wall of 15 as it moves past. (A)

The balls A and A' which may be ping pong or styrofoam balls less than 1" in
diameter are floated on streams of air ejected from tubes B and B' which are
connected to the hollow sphere C. The sphere C may be pressurized by means of a
balloon (D) or by a pump P feeding air thru a line L. and then thru base D into
C. A rotary seal in accordance with my (Fig. 5 patent # 2654973 may be provided
between C and D and the assembly which includes C, B and

when pressed there against. Reference is made to page 11 of Dec. 1957, issue of
Product Design & Development for a more complete description of the properties
of Prelon which has primary use in self-inked marking devices. The Dec 1957
issue of Factory shows a halftone printed impression using Porelon, lipstick
dispenser, use as a battery, filter, deodorizer, etc; lubrication, etc. Product
